# ai-cli-zoo

A curated, deeply-annotated catalog comparing **597 AI coding CLIs**.

[yq](clis/yq/),
[fx](clis/fx/),
[gitu](clis/gitu/). Each entry
is hand-written from real usage, not marketing copy. The goal: help you pick
the right tool for the job in under five minutes.

> **Scope.** This repo only covers CLIs / TUIs that take natural-language
> instructions and edit code on disk. Browser-only assistants and IDE-locked
> plugins are out of scope.

## Contents

| Path | What it is |
|------|------------|
| [`clis/`](clis/) | One subdirectory per tool with a deep README |
| [`CHOOSING.md`](CHOOSING.md) | Decision tree: pick a CLI from your situation |
| [`ARCHITECTURE-PATTERNS.md`](ARCHITECTURE-PATTERNS.md) | Cross-cutting analysis: agent loops, context, tool call shapes, sandboxing |

## The catalog

| CLI | Lang | License | Models | MCP | Sub-agents | Telemetry default | Killer feature |
|-----|------|---------|--------|-----|-----------|--------|------|
| [opencode](clis/opencode/) | TS | MIT | Anthropic, OpenAI, local, OpenRouter, Bedrock | Yes (client + server) | Task tool spawns sub-agents | Off | Skill system + first-class plugin host |
| [codex](clis/codex/) | Rust | Apache-2.0 | OpenAI o-series, GPT-4.1/5 | Yes (client) | Single agent, parallel tool calls | Opt-in | Sandboxed exec via Seatbelt/Landlock |
| [aider](clis/aider/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | Anthropic, OpenAI, Gemini, Ollama, 100+ via litellm | No (built-in repo-map instead) | No | Off | Repo-map + git-native edit/commit loop |
| [cline](clis/cline/) | TS (VS Code) | Apache-2.0 | Anthropic, OpenAI, Bedrock, Vertex, OpenRouter, local | Yes (client + marketplace) | Plan/Act mode, no sub-agents | Off | Approve-each-step trust UX |
| [OpenHands](clis/openhands/) | Python | MIT | LiteLLM-routed (any) | Yes (client) | Multi-agent (CodeAct, browsing, etc.) | Opt-in | Full Linux sandbox + browser agent |
| [crush](clis/crush/) | Go | FSL-1.1-MIT | Anthropic, OpenAI, local | Yes (client) | No | Off | Beautiful TUI, fast Go binary |
| [continue](clis/continue/) | TS | Apache-2.0 | All major + custom | Yes (client) | No | Off | YAML config + reusable prompt blocks |
| [plandex](clis/plandex/) | Go | AGPL/MIT-dual | Anthropic, OpenAI | No | Internal planner / builder split | Opt-in | Long-horizon plans with branching |
| [mentat](clis/mentat/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | OpenAI, Anthropic | No | No | Off | Multi-file edits with diff preview |
| [gptme](clis/gptme/) | Python | MIT | Many via litellm + local | No (tool-based shell) | No | Off | Shell + Python + browser tools in one REPL |
| [smol-developer](clis/smol-developer/) | Python | MIT | OpenAI | No | No | Off | "One prompt → whole repo" greenfield generator |
| [sweep](clis/sweep/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | OpenAI, Anthropic | No | Issue → PR pipeline | Opt-in | GitHub-issue-driven auto-PRs |
| [goose](clis/goose/) | Rust | Apache-2.0 | Anthropic, OpenAI, Gemini, local, Bedrock, Vertex | Yes (client + server, all built-ins are MCP) | Recipe-based composition; subagent extension spawns child process | Opt-in | Everything-is-an-MCP-extension architecture |
| [gemini-cli](clis/gemini-cli/) | TS (Node) | Apache-2.0 | Gemini 2.x / 1.5 (OAuth, AI Studio, Vertex) | Yes (client) | Single agent, parallel tool calls | Opt-in (free tier opts into training) | 1M+ token context with aggressive prefix caching |
| [claude-code](clis/claude-code/) | TS (Node) | Source-available (Anthropic Commercial) | Claude Opus / Sonnet / Haiku (API, Pro/Max OAuth, Bedrock, Vertex) | Yes (client, deeply integrated) | True sub-agents via `Task` tool, configurable per project | Opt-out (no content training on API/Pro/Max) | Hooks + Skills + Sub-agents triangle |
| [mods](clis/mods/) | Go | MIT | OpenAI, Anthropic, Gemini, Cohere, Groq, local, Azure, any OpenAI-compatible | No | None — one-shot stdin→stdout | Off (no telemetry at all) | Unix-pipe primitive for LLMs |
| [forge](clis/forge/) | Rust (npm launcher) | Apache-2.0 | Anthropic, OpenAI, Gemini, OpenRouter, local, any OpenAI-compatible | Yes (client) | YAML-defined multi-agent workflows, per-step model | Off | Provider-mixing as a first-class concept (planner / editor / reviewer on different models) |
| [qwen-code](clis/qwen-code/) | TS (Node) | Apache-2.0 | Qwen3-Coder (OAuth + DashScope), any OpenAI-compatible endpoint | Yes (client) | Single agent, parallel tool calls | Opt-in | First-party Qwen3-Coder access with a real free-tier quota |
| [llm](clis/llm/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | OpenAI built-in; Anthropic, Gemini, Mistral, Cohere, Ollama, OpenRouter, Bedrock, etc. via plugins | Plugin-only (experimental `llm-tools-mcp`) | None — single conversation | Off (no telemetry) | SQLite log of every prompt/response + first-class plugin system |
| [aichat](clis/aichat/) | Rust | MIT/Apache-2.0 | 20+ providers built-in: OpenAI, Anthropic, Gemini, Mistral, Cohere, Groq, DeepSeek, Together, Ollama, Bedrock, Qwen/Zhipu/Moonshot/Ernie, any OpenAI-compatible | No (function-script convention instead) | None — serial function calls | Off (no telemetry) | Single static binary with built-in document RAG + shell-integration completion |
| [open-interpreter](clis/open-interpreter/) | Python | AGPL-3.0 | OpenAI, Anthropic, Gemini, local (Ollama/LM Studio/llama.cpp), any OpenAI-compatible via litellm | No | None — single REPL with code-exec loop | Off (opt-in) | Code-execution REPL: model writes Python/shell, runs it locally, sees output, loops |
| [shell-gpt](clis/shell-gpt/) | Python | MIT | OpenAI built-in; anything OpenAI-compatible (LiteLLM proxies, Ollama, LM Studio, vLLM) | No | None — flat chat sessions, OpenAI-style functions | Off (no telemetry) | `Ctrl-L` shell integration: natural-language → shell command with [E]xecute/[D]escribe/[A]bort prompt |
| [tgpt](clis/tgpt/) | Go | GPL-3.0 | Free providers (Pollinations, Phind, DuckDuckGo, Blackbox, Koboldai) by default; OpenAI/Anthropic/Groq/Ollama/OpenRouter via flags | No | None — one-shot or flat REPL | Off (no telemetry; free providers see prompts) | Zero-config no-API-key terminal LLM; `brew install tgpt && tgpt "..."` works in 30 seconds |
| [fabric](clis/fabric/) | Go | MIT | OpenAI, Anthropic, Gemini, Groq, Ollama, OpenRouter, Azure, Bedrock | No | None — one pattern = one call, compose via shell pipes | Off (no telemetry) | Shared, version-controlled, hand-curated 200+ pattern library as the product |
| [files-to-prompt](clis/files-to-prompt/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | None — emits text for downstream LLM CLI | No | None — context packer, not a model client | Off (no network) | Deterministic context packer for piping into any LLM CLI; honors `.gitignore`, emits Anthropic XML / markdown / line-numbered shapes |
| [oterm](clis/oterm/) | Python | MIT | Ollama only (whatever `ollama list` reports) | Yes (client) | None — chat tabs with in-line tool calls | Off (no network beyond Ollama) | Persistent multi-tab Textual TUI purpose-built for local Ollama, with edit-and-fork on every turn |
| [gorilla-cli](clis/gorilla-cli/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | Hosted Gorilla endpoint by default; any OpenAI-compatible endpoint via `GORILLA_API_URL` | No | None — one HTTP call returns N candidates | On (hosted endpoint logs prompts) | Multi-candidate shell-command picker with arrow-key selection; zero-key default, shell-only scope |
| [opencommit](clis/opencommit/) | TS (Node) | MIT | OpenAI, Anthropic, Azure, Gemini, Groq, Mistral, Ollama, any OpenAI-compatible | No | None — one LLM call per commit | Off (no analytics) | `prepare-commit-msg` git-hook integration: `git commit` opens `$EDITOR` with a Conventional-Commits-shaped message pre-filled from the staged diff |
| [aicommits](clis/aicommits/) | TS (Node) | MIT | OpenAI built-in; any OpenAI-compatible endpoint via `OPENAI_API_BASE` (Ollama, vLLM, LiteLLM, Groq, OpenRouter) | No | None — one diff → N suggestions | Off (no telemetry) | `-g N` multi-suggestion picker: arrow-key choose between N candidate commit messages instead of edit-or-confirm a single one |
| [aiac](clis/aiac/) | Go | Apache-2.0 | OpenAI, Azure, Anthropic, Bedrock, Ollama, any OpenAI-compatible | No | None — chat mode is single-thread | Off (no analytics) | IaC-shaped post-processing: emits clean Terraform / Pulumi / K8s / Dockerfile / GitHub Actions artifacts ready to `fmt && validate`, no markdown fences or prose |
| [symbex](clis/symbex/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | None — emits Python source for downstream LLM CLI | No | None — AST extractor, not a model client | Off (no network) | AST-correct surgical symbol extractor: `symbex 'MyClass.*'` prints exactly the matching Python methods, an order-of-magnitude smaller context than file-level packers |
| [repomix](clis/repomix/) | TS (Node) | MIT | None — emits text; tokenizes with `tiktoken` | Yes (server: `repomix --mcp`) | None — one-shot pack | Off (no analytics) | Remote-fetch + Tree-sitter compression + Secretlint secret-scan + per-directory token counts in one packer; `repomix --remote owner/repo --compress` works without cloning |
| [chatblade](clis/chatblade/) | Python | MIT | OpenAI built-in; any OpenAI-compatible endpoint via `OPENAI_API_BASE` (Ollama, vLLM, LM Studio, LiteLLM, OpenRouter, Azure) | No | None — one round-trip per call | Off (no analytics) | Inline structured-output extraction: `chatblade -e '.commands[0]' -j "..."` makes the model reply as JSON and pulls out a sub-path in one command, plus plain-text named sessions you can `git diff` |
| [promptfoo](clis/promptfoo/) | TS (Node) | MIT | OpenAI, Anthropic, Gemini, Bedrock, Ollama, Replicate, HuggingFace, custom HTTP / Python | No (custom-provider hook instead) | None — eval harness, not an agent | Off (eval cache local; `share` opt-in) | Cartesian-product prompt eval: `prompts × providers × tests` with assertions (`contains`, `is-json`, `latency`, `cost`, `llm-rubric`, `javascript`/`python`), HTML diff viewer, optional red-team mode |
| [marker](clis/marker/) | Python | GPL/commercial-dual | None for core (layout/OCR/table local models); optional `--use_llm` finishing pass via OpenAI / Anthropic / Gemini / Ollama | No | None — converter, not an agent | Off (network only if `--use_llm` configured) | PDF / EPUB / DOCX → clean Markdown with preserved tables, LaTeX equations, and image refs; the missing front-end for every other CLI in this catalog |
| [gptscript](clis/gptscript/) | Go | Apache-2.0 | OpenAI, Anthropic, Azure, any OpenAI-compatible | Yes (client; tools can be MCP servers, OpenAPI specs, or other `.gpt` files) | Sub-tools: scripts call other scripts as tools | Off | `.gpt` files: English instruction body + declared tools / args / output schema, runnable and composable like shell scripts |
| [shell-genie](clis/shell-genie/) | Python | MIT | OpenAI built-in; hosted free `free-genie` endpoint; any OpenAI-compatible endpoint via `OPENAI_API_BASE` | No | None — one HTTP call per ask | Off (no analytics; `feedback` writes locally only) | Aggressively minimal natural-language → one shell command → y/n; ships shell-aware prompt templates for bash / zsh / fish / PowerShell |
| [elia](clis/elia/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | OpenAI, Anthropic, Gemini, Groq, Ollama, any OpenAI-compatible (declared in `config.toml`) | No | None — linear chat threads | Off (no telemetry; history stays in local SQLite) | Multi-provider Textual chat TUI with persistent SQLite history, `/`-search across past conversations, and `Ctrl-J` mid-conversation model switching |
| [khoj](clis/khoj/) | Python | AGPL-3.0 | Embed: local sentence-transformers or OpenAI; Chat: local llama.cpp/Ollama, OpenAI, Anthropic, Gemini, any OpenAI-compatible | No (HTTP API only) | User-facing personas, not autonomous sub-agents | Off with `--anonymous-mode`; opt-in account telemetry otherwise | Long-lived local daemon that incrementally indexes a personal corpus (notes, PDFs, code) and answers chat queries with citations, fully offline-capable |
| [code-review-gpt](clis/code-review-gpt/) | TS (Node) | MIT | OpenAI, Anthropic, any OpenAI-compatible | No | None — one LLM call per file | Off (no analytics) | Diff-scoped PR-time AI code review with a CI mode that posts inline GitHub PR comments; custom rubrics encode team-specific lint policy that regex linters cannot express |
| [logai](clis/logai/) | Python | BSD-3-Clause | Local: TF-IDF / Word2Vec / sentence-transformers; LLM summarization (optional): OpenAI, any OpenAI-compatible | No | None — sequential pipeline stages | Off (no analytics; LLM egress only if summarization enabled) | Two-stage log analysis: classical Drain/IPLoM template extraction + Isolation Forest anomaly scoring collapses GBs to dozens of templates, then LLM summarizes only the residual anomalies |
| [txtai](clis/txtai/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | Embeddings: sentence-transformers, OpenAI, Cohere, HF; LLM: local llama.cpp/Ollama, OpenAI, Anthropic, any LiteLLM-routed | No (FastAPI surface available) | None — linear YAML workflows | Off (no analytics; fully offline by default) | Index-as-a-file portability: build an embeddings index on one machine, scp the tarball, query offline with the same CLI; covers vector search + graph-RAG + HF pipelines behind one shell surface |
| [k8sgpt](clis/k8sgpt/) | Go | Apache-2.0 | Optional `--explain` backend: OpenAI, Azure, Cohere, Bedrock, Vertex, HuggingFace, LocalAI, Ollama, `noopai` | No (gRPC `serve` instead) | None — analyzers run in parallel, one sweep per `analyze` | Off (no analytics; LLM egress only when `--explain` set) | Deterministic Kubernetes analyzer catalog (Pods, Services, Ingress, HPAs, webhooks, gateways…) finds breakage on its own; LLM is a post-hoc narration layer for on-call humans, not the decision-maker |
| [ttok](clis/ttok/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | None — `tiktoken` encoder only; `-m gpt-4o` selects a tokenizer, not an endpoint | No | None — one-shot tokenizer | Off (one-time vocab download from OpenAI's public CDN, then offline) | Cheap pre-flight token gate for every other catalog packer: `… \| ttok` answers "will this fit?" before paying for an API call, `… \| ttok --truncate N` caps the stream |
| [strip-tags](clis/strip-tags/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | None — emits text for downstream LLM CLI | No | None — HTML→text Unix filter | Off (no network; `strip-tags` does not fetch URLs itself) | HTML→text cleaner that drops `<script>`/`<style>`/chrome and supports `bs4` CSS selectors; the missing front-end for "I just `curl`'d a webpage and want to ask the model about it" without burning tokens on tracker JS |
| [tlm](clis/tlm/) | Go | Apache-2.0 | Ollama only (whatever `ollama list` reports) | No | None — one-shot `suggest`/`explain`/`chat` | Off (no telemetry; only egress is your local Ollama endpoint) | Single static Go binary for the local-only natural-language → shell-command loop, with a `tlm install` bootstrap that pulls and configures an Ollama model in one command |
| [smartcat](clis/smartcat/) | Rust | Apache-2.0 | OpenAI, Anthropic, Mistral, Groq, any OpenAI-compatible (Ollama / vLLM / LM Studio / LiteLLM / OpenRouter / DeepSeek) — declared per-block in `.api_configs.toml` | No | None — stdin→stdout filter | Off (no telemetry; conversation file local) | Named system prompts as a `prompts.toml` config file (`sc -p commit < diff.txt`, `sc -p review < diff.txt`) plus first-class glob input (`sc -g 'src/**/*.rs' "..."`) for a Unix-native LLM filter |
| [ramalama](clis/ramalama/) | Python (containerised `llama.cpp`) | Apache-2.0 | Any GGUF model, pulled from Ollama registry, Hugging Face, OCI artifact registries, or local files; no closed-weight cloud models | No (exposes OpenAI-compatible HTTP for MCP-aware clients to point at) | None — runtime layer, not an agent | Off (no telemetry; Podman/Docker pulls visible to those upstreams) | Hardware-aware container selection for local LLM inference: same `pull`/`run`/`serve` UX across CPU, NVIDIA CUDA, AMD ROCm, Intel oneAPI, Apple Metal — pick the matching `llama.cpp` image automatically |
| [magentic](clis/magentic/) | Python | MIT | OpenAI, Anthropic (built-in extras); ~100 more via LiteLLM extra | No | None — single round-trip per `@prompt` call; you drive any tool loop in Python | Off (no analytics; egress only to provider) | Type-annotated structured output as the primary API: `def f(...) -> list[Recipe]` returns validated Pydantic objects, streaming-aware |
| [mentals-ai](clis/mentals-ai/) | C++ | MIT | OpenAI built-in; any OpenAI-compatible endpoint (Ollama, vLLM, LiteLLM, OpenRouter, DeepSeek) | No | Sub-agents as Markdown link syntax (`use:`/`delegate:`) — recursive composition is a language construct | Off (no analytics; local `.log` traces) | Markdown-as-program: the agent definition *is* a `.md` file with `# Heading` mentals, runnable as a graph by a single C++ binary |
| [ai-shell](clis/ai-shell/) | TS (Node) | MIT | OpenAI built-in; any OpenAI-compatible endpoint via `OPENAI_API_ENDPOINT` (Ollama, LiteLLM, vLLM, OpenRouter, Groq, DeepSeek) | No | None — one-shot translator with optional `ai chat` REPL | Off (no analytics; OpenAI endpoint sees prompts) | `[E]xecute / [R]evise / [C]opy` revise loop on every suggestion: iterate the shell command without retyping the original intent |
| [code2prompt](clis/code2prompt/) | Rust | MIT | None — emits text for downstream LLM CLI | Yes (server: `code2prompt --mcp`) | None — one-shot packer | Off (no telemetry; only egress is the clipboard / output file) | Single static Rust binary that packs a tree into a prompt with **Handlebars templates** for the export shape, plus an interactive TUI with a live `tiktoken` counter so you can hand-curate context against a token budget before exporting |
| [wut](clis/wut/) | Python | MIT | OpenAI, Anthropic, Ollama (env-var configured) | No | None — one LLM call per invocation | Off (no analytics; provider sees the scrollback you just printed) | Reads your **current `tmux` / `screen` pane scrollback** and explains the last command's output — three keystrokes, zero copy-paste, optional follow-up question |
| [micro-agent](clis/micro-agent/) | TS (Node) | MIT | OpenAI, Anthropic, any OpenAI-compatible (Ollama, Groq, vLLM, LiteLLM, OpenRouter) | No | Two-agent in `--visual` mode (Claude critiques, OpenAI writes); single agent otherwise | Off (no analytics; provider sees source + tests + test output) | **The failing test is the halting condition**: agent rewrites a single file until `npm test` (or whatever `-t` is) passes, capped at `--max-runs N` — observable stop condition instead of "model says done" |
| [ollama](clis/ollama/) | Go | MIT | Any GGUF from the Ollama library or imported via `Modelfile`: Llama 3.x, Qwen 2.5 / 2.5-Coder, Gemma 2/3, DeepSeek-V3 / Coder / R1, Phi-4, Mistral / Mixtral, Granite-Code, embedding & vision models; no closed-weight cloud models | No (exposes OpenAI-compatible HTTP at `:11434/v1` for MCP-aware clients to point at) | None — runtime layer, not an agent | Off (no telemetry; only egress is the Ollama registry on `pull` and your own clients on `:11434`) | The path of least resistance to "I have a local LLM on this laptop": `brew install ollama && ollama run llama3.1` works in under five minutes, then becomes the substrate every other catalog entry's "any OpenAI-compatible endpoint" cell points at |
| [llm-cmd](clis/llm-cmd/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | Inherits from [`llm`](clis/llm/) — OpenAI built-in plus Anthropic / Gemini / Mistral / Cohere / Ollama / OpenRouter / Bedrock via plugins | No | None — one prompt → one model call → one suggested command | Off (inherits `llm`'s no-telemetry posture; every call logged to local SQLite via `llm logs`) | Suggestion lands in your **readline buffer** as if you'd typed it — no TUI dialog, no `[E]xecute/[D]escribe` menu; your shell's normal line editor (readline / zle / fish) handles edit-then-Enter |
| [gitingest](clis/gitingest/) | Python | MIT | None — emits text for downstream LLM CLI; tokenizes with `tiktoken` | No | None — one-shot packer | Off (CLI does not phone home; remote fetches go directly to GitHub; hosted `gitingest.com` web mirror is opt-in) | `gitingest <github-url>` (or `owner/repo`) packs a remote repo without a local clone, and the same engine runs at `gitingest.com` so a teammate without the CLI can grab the same digest by URL-renaming `hub` → `ingest` |

spans contain prompts + completions by default — apply `span_processor` redaction filters for sensitive workloads | **One line, every framework, dollar-accurate cost per session** — `agentops.init(api_key=os.environ["AGENTOPS_API_KEY"])` above your `crew.kickoff()` / `Runner.run(agent)` / `graph.invoke(...)` turns the next run into a viewable trace with **per-LLM-event USD spend computed from a maintained provider price table** (~50 providers + ~200 models including frontier reasoning tiers and provider-specific input / cached-input / output / reasoning-token pricing); for multi-agent crews this is the one number stakeholders actually ask for ("how much does one customer-support session cost?") and it lands without you writing a token-counter wrapper around every provider's SDK; session-replay view (full message tree + tool I/O + token counts + per-step latency waterfall) is the debugger of choice when a CrewAI / Agno run goes off the rails |

| [docsgpt](clis/docsgpt/) | Python (Flask + Celery) + TypeScript (React) | MIT | OpenAI for chat + embeddings by default; switchable via `LLM_PROVIDER=ollama` / `LLM_PROVIDER=llama.cpp` / `LLM_PROVIDER=docsgpt` (bundled tiny model) or any OpenAI-compatible endpoint via `OPENAI_BASE_URL`; vector stores: FAISS default, Qdrant / Milvus / Mongo / Elastic / Pinecone supported | Yes (client) — agent builder mounts external MCP servers as tools alongside the built-in catalog (web search, Python sandbox, OpenAPI callout, TTS, image gen, scheduled deep research); no first-party MCP server flavour exposing the corpus outward | Implicit — the deep-research tool runs a planner LLM that emits sub-questions, each sub-question becomes a separate search-and-read sub-call against the source set, and a synthesis pass collapses them; not exposed as user-facing nested-agent CLI | Off by default in OSS self-host (back-end does not phone home; LLM and embedding providers see prompts + documents per their own posture; pair with Ollama + self-hosted vector store for fully air-gapped); hosted `app.docsgpt.cloud` is the opt-in cloud surface | **No-code agent builder layered on top of a real source-and-vector-store ingestion pipeline, with a ready-made Chrome extension and Chatwoot bridge for non-technical end-users** — most catalog RAG tools stop at "you get an HTTP endpoint, build your own UI"; DocsGPT ships the UI, the multi-source ingestion (Confluence / Notion / GitHub / Drive / S3 / web crawl), the agent builder, and the distribution surfaces (web app + Chrome + Discord + Chatwoot) in one MIT repo, so "let support agents query our docs corpus from inside Chatwoot" goes from one-quarter to one-afternoon |

Model-graded scorers issue one OpenAI-compatible chat call against whatever client you pass (`openai` / `litellm` / `anthropic` / Azure / Bedrock / a local `vllm` / `ollama` endpoint via the OpenAI shim); heuristic scorers (`Levenshtein`, `JSONDiff`, `EmbeddingSimilarity`, `NumericDiff`, `ExactMatch`) issue zero LLM calls | No — scoring primitive; an MCP server wrapping `score_factuality` / `score_answer_relevancy` is a small adapter | None — pure callable scorers; one LLM call per `(input, output, expected)` triple for model-graded; batch parallelism is the caller's responsibility (`concurrent.futures` / `asyncio.gather`) | Off — only egress is the LLM call you configure; no analytics, no Sentry, no hosted phone-home; the sibling Braintrust eval platform is a separate opt-in package | **The standard set of LLM scoring functions (`Factuality`, `AnswerRelevancy`, `AnswerCorrectness`, `Battle`, `ClosedQA`, `Possible`, `Security`, `Sql`, `Translation`, `LLMClassifier` builder over Chevron prompts, plus heuristic `Levenshtein` / `JSONDiff` / `EmbeddingSimilarity`) as plain MIT callables in Python *and* TypeScript with parity** — every scorer returns `Score(name, score in 0..1, metadata, rationale)` from a uniform `(input?, output, expected?, **kwargs)` signature; the layer underneath gating-shaped harnesses ([`promptfoo`](clis/promptfoo/), [`deepeval`](clis/deepeval/)) that wrap a copy of these scorers anyway, dropped into pytest / a notebook / a CI step / a custom eval loop without adopting a project shape; `LLMClassifier(name="...", prompt_template="...", choice_scores={"A": 1, "B": 0})` is the entire shape for a custom rubric |
| [datachain](clis/datachain/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | Not a model — multimodal dataset library. UDFs call any Python: `openai`, `anthropic`, `litellm`, `transformers`, `sentence-transformers`, local CLIP / Whisper / YOLO, or a local Ollama / vLLM endpoint via the OpenAI shim; storage backends: SQLite (default), Postgres, ClickHouse for the metadata catalog; data plane: S3 / GCS / Azure / local FS referenced by content-addressed manifest | No — headless data library; an MCP server exposing `datachain query` is a small adapter | None — `Chain` is a lazy DAG of `gen` (1→N) / `map` (1→1) / `filter` / `agg` / `save` operators that compile to one query plan; concurrency is a thread / process pool over UDF rows with checkpoint-and-resume into the catalog so a 10 TB enrichment pass survives an OOM mid-run | Anonymous Iterative-style telemetry (run counts, no row content); opt-out via `STUDIO_TOKEN` config or `DATACHAIN_NO_ANALYTICS=1`; egress = whichever LLM / embedding endpoint your UDFs call + the object-storage bucket you read from | **The data-engineering peer to [`dvc`](https://dvc.org) for the unstructured-data + LLM-annotation era — pandas / polars-shaped operators (`map`, `filter`, `agg`) over images / video / audio / PDFs with content-addressed dataset versioning that handles 10 TB corpora in seconds without copying bytes**; UDFs declare their input columns with type hints, Pydantic models become row schemas, and the result is one diffable Python file per dataset version (`my_dataset.py` + `datachain query my_dataset.py`) that a coding-agent CLI can author and re-run; the headless / SQL-shaped counterpart to [`fiftyone`](clis/fiftyone/)'s App-in-the-loop visual-AI workflow |

| [prefect](clis/prefect/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | Not a model — workflow orchestrator. `@flow` / `@task` decorators wrap any Python; tasks happily call OpenAI / Anthropic / litellm / local Ollama / vLLM endpoints, HF datasets, S3, Snowflake, dbt — orchestration is provider-agnostic | No (orchestrator surface — REST API at `:4200/api`, Python SDK, CLI; an MCP server exposing `prefect deployment run` / `prefect flow-run logs` is a small adapter) | None — `@flow` is the unit; sub-flows are just nested `@flow` calls; concurrency is `task.submit()` against a `ConcurrentTaskRunner` / `DaskTaskRunner` / `RayTaskRunner`; retries / timeouts / caching are decorator kwargs (`@task(retries=3, retry_delay_seconds=10, cache_key_fn=…)`) | Off when running the OSS server (`prefect server start` → local SQLite at `~/.prefect/`); `prefect cloud login` opts into Prefect's SaaS metadata plane; egress = whichever providers your tasks call | **The decorator-shaped peer to [`dagster`](clis/dagster/) for Python AI / data pipelines that don't justify Airflow — the same `@flow` you call interactively in a notebook is what `prefect worker` runs in production on a cron / interval / RRULE schedule, retries / caching / concurrency are kwargs not YAML, and the local-SQLite → managed-Postgres upgrade path is a connection-string swap**; v3.x rewrote the engine and replaced `agent` with pull-based `worker` pools, so any tutorial that says `prefect agent start` is v2 and will not work; pairs naturally with [`modal`](clis/modal/) (a `@flow` whose tasks call `modal.Function.lookup(...).remote(...)`) and the experiment trackers ([`mlflow`](clis/mlflow/), [`aim`](clis/aim/), [`trackio`](clis/trackio/)) for end-to-end ML scheduling |

| [sqlite-utils](clis/sqlite-utils/) | Python | Apache-2.0 | Not a model — SQLite Swiss-army CLI; emits JSON / CSV / TSV / NL-JSON for downstream LLM CLI tools | No — one-shot CLI; programmable surface is `import sqlite_utils` Python API for in-process use | None — flat shell commands (`insert`, `query`, `transform`, `extract`, `enable-fts`, `memory`, `schema`, `rows`, `views`, `triggers`, `analyze`); `memory` loads CSV / JSON args as anonymous tables for one-shot SQL with no DB at all; concurrency is "run more shell processes" | Off — no telemetry, no network; only egress is the SQLite file you wrote | **The shortest path from "I have a file" to "I have a queryable database" — `sqlite-utils insert mydata.db events events.csv --csv --detect-types` creates the table, infers column types, and bulk-inserts in one call; `sqlite-utils memory access.csv "select status, count(*) from t group by 1"` runs SQL against a CSV without ever materializing a file; `transform` mutates schemas in place (rebuilding under the hood since SQLite has no full `ALTER`); `enable-fts` adds an FTS5 index with optional sync triggers**; the upstream loader / schema-mutator that produces the `.db` other tools open ([`datasette`](clis/datasette/) serves it, [`harlequin`](clis/harlequin/) edits it interactively); for LLM workflows, `sqlite-utils insert prompts.db runs out.json` is the canonical way to land an LLM CLI's JSON output into a queryable log without writing any Python; sister project `db-to-sqlite` handles Postgres / MySQL ingestion |

| [tach](clis/tach/) | Python CLI + Rust core (PyO3) | MIT | Not a model — static analyzer; parses Python `import` statements into a module graph and enforces declared edges from `tach.toml`; no LLM in the loop | No — CI-shaped lint tool; programmable surface is `import tach` Python API for in-process use, and the parseable `tach check --output json` for downstream consumption | None — flat shell commands (`mod`, `sync`, `check`, `show`, `report`, `test`); the relevant primitive is **the declared dependency graph** in `tach.toml` and the per-module `depends_on` list; concurrency is the Rust core parallelising AST parses across CPU cores | Off — pure local static analysis, no network, no telemetry, no phone-home | **The "import-linter that you actually adopt" for Python — `tach mod` lists modules, `tach sync` infers the *current* dependency edges as the baseline, `tach check` fails CI on undeclared imports, so a growing Python codebase gets the layered-architecture hygiene Java / Go / Rust have by default**; the Rust core (PyO3-bound) parses tens of thousands of files per second so the check is cheap enough for every PR run, `tach show --format mermaid` exports the graph for documentation, and `tach test --base origin/main` runs only the tests downstream of the diff (the Python answer to `bazel query`) |

| [lazygit](clis/lazygit/) | Go | MIT | Not a model — git TUI client; shells out to the system `git` binary, respects `~/.gitconfig`, optional integration with `gh` / `glab` for PR creation and `delta` / `diff-so-fancy` for diff rendering | No — local TUI; programmable surface is the `customCommands:` YAML DSL in `~/.config/lazygit/config.yml` for project-specific keybinds (each invokes a shell command with prompts / confirms / variable substitution) | None — single-process TUI; concurrency is "open another terminal pane"; the operation log (`z` to undo) only undoes operations `lazygit` performed itself this session | Off — no telemetry, no analytics, no phone-home; only egress is whatever `git push` / `git fetch` / `gh pr create` you fire from inside the UI | **Five-panel ncurses-style TUI (status / files / branches / commits / stash) where every common git operation is one or two keystrokes — per-hunk + per-line staging without `git add -p`'s modal prompts, interactive rebase as a live editable TUI (`s` squash, `f` fixup, `d` drop, `Ctrl+J/K` reorder), three-way conflict resolution with picker UI instead of conflict markers in your editor**; for an LLM-CLI workflow that produces frequent small commits that need squashing / reordering / amending before push, collapses the "clean up the history before push" step from minutes to seconds; pairs naturally with [`delta`](clis/delta/) (set `core.pager = delta` and lazygit's diff modals render through it) and [`gh`](https://cli.github.com/) (`o` on a branch shells out to `gh pr create`) |
| [delta](clis/delta/) | Rust | MIT | Not a model — diff pager; consumes `git diff` / `git log -p` / `git show` / `git blame` / `git stash show -p` output (and bare `diff -u`, `rg --json`, working-tree merge conflict markers) and re-renders with `syntect`-based syntax highlighting against any Sublime `.tmTheme` | No — output renderer; programmable surface is the `[delta]` section of `~/.gitconfig` (features, side-by-side, line-numbers, navigate, syntax-theme, custom regex matchers) | None — pure pipe filter; one-shot per invocation; the wiring point is `git config --global core.pager delta` so every paginated git command runs through it | Off — no telemetry, no network, no phone-home; only egress is the bundled syntax-grammar set on first run (cached in the binary) | **The diff pager you wire into `core.pager` once and never think about again — side-by-side layout for long moved blocks (a 50-line function moved between files becomes readable instead of a wall of `-` followed by a wall of `+`), `syntect` syntax highlighting that actually parses the language on each `+` / `-` line (Rust lifetimes, Python f-strings, TSX, Markdown all colored correctly), three-way merge conflict rendering (ours / base / theirs in three columns instead of `<<<<<<<` markers in your editor), and `delta.navigate = true` adds `n` / `N` keybinds to jump between hunks**; pairs with [`lazygit`](clis/lazygit/) / [`gitui`](clis/gitui/) (set `core.pager = delta` and their diff modals render through it) and orthogonal to [`bat`](clis/bat/) (which highlights source files, not diff structure) |
| [jj](clis/jj/) | Rust | Apache-2.0 | Not a model — git-compatible VCS; backed by either a native Jujutsu store or a git store (`jj git init --colocate` makes `.jj/` and `.git/` co-exist so teammates on plain git clone / pull / push normally) | No — VCS; programmable surface is the `~/.jjconfig.toml` template engine (custom `jj log` revsets, custom command aliases, formatter hooks via `jj fix`, integration with editors / shells / mergetools) | None — operation log (`jj op log`) records every repo-modifying operation and `jj op restore <op-id>` rolls the entire repo back to that operation's state including working copy + bookmarks (the universal undo); concurrency is one working copy per checkout (use `jj workspace add` for multi-checkout) | Off — pure local VCS; no telemetry; only egress is `jj git push` / `jj git fetch` against whichever git remote you configure | **The git-compatible VCS that fixes git's commit model — every working-tree edit is automatically a commit (no `add` / `commit` cycle), the operation log is a queryable history (`jj op restore` rolls back any aborted rebase including the working copy), conflicts are first-class commit content (a `jj rebase` over a conflicting change *succeeds* — the resulting "conflicted commit" can be rebased / split / abandoned without resolving first), and change IDs (stable across rewrites) are separate from commit IDs (which change on every rewrite) so `jj rebase` / `jj squash` / `jj split` don't break references**; `--colocate` mode means a `jj`-managed repo is also a normal git repo every teammate can use with plain `git`, so adoption is per-individual not per-team; for an LLM-CLI workflow that produces a long stack of small related commits needing frequent reorder / squash / split, removes most of the friction; orthogonal to [`lazygit`](clis/lazygit/) / [`gitui`](clis/gitui/) (those are UIs on git, this is a different VCS — they don't compose) |
| [zellij](clis/zellij/) | Rust | MIT | Not a model — terminal multiplexer; runs any shell / REPL / TUI inside its panes; renders the host terminal's native graphics protocol when child programs emit them | No — local multiplexer; programmable surface is the KDL layout language (`~/.config/zellij/layouts/*.kdl`) for declarative pane / tab / command-on-start workspaces, plus a WebAssembly plugin runtime where built-in widgets (status bar, tab bar, session manager) are themselves wasm modules and third-party plugins drop in as `*.wasm` files | None — sessions are per-host; multiplexing is panes / tabs / floating panes within one zellij server process; `zellij --layout dev` boots a declared workspace deterministically; `Ctrl+O d` detaches a session and `zellij attach <name>` reattaches across SSH disconnects | Off — no telemetry, no analytics, no phone-home; only egress is whatever the child programs in your panes do | **The `tmux`-class terminal multiplexer with `tmux`'s onboarding cliff filed off — visible status / tab bar by default, the bottom strip lists the keys for the current mode (`NORMAL` / `PANE` / `TAB` / `RESIZE` / `SCROLL` / `SESSION` / `LOCKED`) so workflows are discoverable not memorized, `Ctrl+G` lock-mode passes every key through to the inner program for editor-keymap conflicts, layouts are KDL files (declarative, diffable in git, one-command boot of "editor + log tail + REPL + git status" workspaces), and the wasm plugin runtime makes third-party panes (richer status bars, keybind helpers, fullscreen-with-search) drop in as one file**; pairs with [`lazygit`](clis/lazygit/) / [`yazi`](clis/yazi/) / [`bottom`](clis/bottom/) (run each in its own pane, switch with one keystroke) and orthogonal to `tmux` (pick zellij when discoverability + KDL layouts + wasm plugins beat `tmux`'s ubiquity + plugin-catalog maturity) |
| [yazi](clis/yazi/) | Rust | MIT | Not a model — async terminal file manager; previews text via built-in renderer, images via the host terminal's native graphics protocol (`kitty`, `iterm2`, `sixel`, `chafa` fallback), archives via listing, and arbitrary types via on-disk opener rules in `yazi.toml` | No — TUI; programmable surface is the on-disk DSL (`keymap.toml` for keybinds, `yazi.toml` for openers / theme / preview rules) plus a Lua plugin runtime (`~/.config/yazi/plugins/<name>.yazi/`) for git-status overlays, smart-enter, archive passthrough, chmod modals; `ya` companion CLI is the IPC surface for "tell the running yazi to reveal `/path/to/file`" | None — single-process TUI with a Tokio async runtime so directory reads / image previews / archive scans / plugin calls never block the UI; concurrency is "open another tab inside yazi" (`Ctrl+t`) or "open another yazi pane in your multiplexer" | Off — no telemetry, no analytics, no phone-home; only egress is whatever opener you invoke from the file you focused | **The `ranger`-class file manager rewritten async-first — three-column TUI (parent dir / current dir / preview) where cursoring onto a 100k-entry directory or a slow network mount never freezes the UI (loading state + update-when-ready instead of block-the-event-loop), inline image previews via the terminal's native graphics protocol with no `ueberzug` daemon, bulk-rename via `$EDITOR` (select with `space` / `v`, hit `:` rename, edit the names in vim, save, yazi applies the diff), Lua plugin runtime + on-disk keybind / opener DSL so customization is a config file not a recompile**; pairs with [`zellij`](clis/zellij/) (run yazi in one pane and your editor in another) and the shell wrapper that `cd`s the parent shell to wherever yazi exited turns "navigate visually, then drop back to the right shell prompt" into a one-keystroke flow |
| [just](clis/just/) | Rust | CC0-1.0 | Not a model — project-local command runner; reads a `justfile` (one per repo) and runs declared recipes; per-recipe shebang lines let any single recipe be Python / Node / `nu` / `bash` instead of POSIX `sh`; `set dotenv-load := true` sources `.env` automatically; OS-conditional `[macos]` / `[linux]` / `[windows]` recipe attributes | No — task runner; programmable surface is the `justfile` DSL itself (typed parameters with defaults, recipe dependencies that chain runs, doc comments that auto-render in `--list`) plus a JSON dump (`--dump --dump-format json`) for tooling that wants to introspect the recipe set | None — sequential recipe execution; concurrency is "run two `just` calls in two terminals"; recipe dependencies always re-run (no mtime-based skip — push the up-to-date check into the underlying tool like `cargo build` which is itself incremental) | Off — no telemetry, no analytics, no phone-home; only egress is whatever the recipes themselves shell out to | **The project-local task runner you check into git — `make` syntax pain (tabs only, `$$` to escape `$`, shell-per-line resets cwd, implicit rules firing when you didn't ask) gone, real argument passing with defaults (`just deploy production` vs `just deploy` defaulting to `staging`), per-recipe shebangs so a recipe can be a Python script without `bash -c heredoc` gymnastics, `--list` auto-help from doc comments, `--choose` opens an fzf picker over recipes — onboarding a new contributor collapses to "clone, run `just`"**; for an LLM-CLI workflow, `justfile` is the right place to formalise the agent-callable surface (`just lint`, `just test`, `just typecheck`, `just fmt-check`) so a `CLAUDE.md` / `AGENTS.md` reference stays stable when the underlying tool swaps from `cargo` to `bazel` or `npm` to `pnpm` |
| [tokei](clis/tokei/) | Rust | MIT OR Apache-2.0 (dual) | Not a model — code-line counter; per-language tokenizer state machines (string-aware, nested-comment-aware) for ~250 languages including modern syntax (Rust raw strings, Swift multi-line literals, Vue / Svelte / MDX SFCs, TSX, Nix, Zig, Gleam) so the `code` vs `comment` vs `blank` split is right on cases where regex-based counters miscount | No — static analyzer; programmable surface is `--output json/yaml/cbor/openmetrics` (the OpenMetrics exporter drops straight into Prometheus pushgateway), `--files` per-file mode for `jq` post-processing, and `.tokeignore` for excluding generated / vendored content beyond `.gitignore` | None — `rayon`-parallel tree walk so a 1M-LOC repo finishes in well under a second on a laptop; the parallelism unit is "one file → one tokenizer pass" | Off — pure local static analysis; no network, no telemetry, no phone-home | **The codebase-size primitive — `cloc` rewritten in Rust, one to two orders of magnitude faster on big repos, more accurate on modern syntax, ships as a static binary instead of a Perl script; sub-second on million-LOC trees so it is cheap enough to run on every PR (track repo growth on a Prometheus dashboard via the OpenMetrics exporter, or two-snapshot diff via `jq` on the JSON output)**; for an LLM-CLI workflow, `tokei -t Rust --files -o json` is the cheapest way to feed an agent the shape of a codebase before asking it to plan refactors — total LOC per file, comment density, language mix — and the JSON drops into a context packer ([`files-to-prompt`](clis/files-to-prompt/), [`code2prompt`](clis/code2prompt/), [`repomix`](clis/repomix/)) as a budget hint |
| [gum](clis/gum/) | Go | MIT | Not a model — TUI widget set exposed as standalone shell commands; each subcommand (`input`, `choose`, `confirm`, `spin`, `filter`, `table`, `write`, `format`, `style`, `file`, `pager`) reads from stdin / argv and writes to stdout, so they compose with shell pipes; theme inheritance via `GUM_*` env vars sourced from `.zshrc` / per-project `gum.env` so the look stays consistent across every script in a repo | No — one widget per process, not a TUI framework; the integration boundary is "argv + env in, exit code + stdout out" so calls from bash / zsh / fish / nu / PowerShell / Makefiles / justfiles / Python `subprocess` / Go `exec.Cmd` all work the same way | None — each `gum` call is a fresh process; for multi-screen stateful UIs you write Bubble Tea proper, not a chain of `gum` invocations | Off — no telemetry, no analytics, no phone-home; only egress is whatever the script around it does | **Polished interactive prompts in shell scripts without leaving shell — every onboarding / deploy / wrapper script eventually grows a `read -p` y/n loop plus an `fzf` invocation for fuzzy-pick plus ANSI escapes for color; `gum` collapses all three into named subcommands with consistent Charm styling so the script stays bash (no Python TUI lib, no Node CLI framework) but feels like a real product** — `gum filter` is fuzzy-filter on stdin, `gum choose --no-limit` is multi-select, `gum input --password` is masked entry, `gum spin --title "deploying..." -- ./deploy.sh` shows a spinner around any wrapped command (exit code propagated), `gum confirm "wipe prod?" && rm -rf …` replaces hand-rolled y/n; for an LLM-CLI workflow, `gum` turns the human-in-the-loop confirmation step from a janky `read -r` into a real picker (`gum choose` the model, `gum input --password` the API key, `gum confirm` the destructive action, `gum spin` while the agent thinks) — five lines of shell, looks like a product |
| [bottom](clis/bottom/) | Rust | MIT | Not a model — system / process / resource monitor; reads OS-native APIs (`/proc` on Linux, `sysctl` / IOKit on macOS, WMI / PDH on Windows, sysctl on FreeBSD); optional NVML for NVIDIA GPU stats on Linux / Windows | No — TUI; programmable surface is the TOML config (`~/.config/bottom/bottom.toml`) where `[[row]]` / `[[row.child]]` blocks declare a tree of widgets with width ratios — the dashboard layout is fully data-driven, multiple layouts are different config files swapped via `--config /path/to/layout.toml` | None — single-process TUI; sampling at fixed intervals (default 1s, configurable to 250ms via `--rate`); `f` freezes / unfreezes the display for reading transient state; `e` expands the focused widget to fullscreen for closer inspection | Off — no telemetry, no analytics, no phone-home; only egress is whatever NVML / sensors / network counters the OS exposes locally | **The cross-platform graphical `htop` — CPU per-core / memory / swap / network rx-tx / temperature / disk IO / battery rendered as braille-character sparklines that look fine in any terminal (no graphics protocol needed), the curve answers "is this CPU spike a runaway, a workload, or a brief blip" before you have to think about it; runs natively on Windows where `htop` does not, with the same keybinds across Linux / macOS / Windows / FreeBSD; process table sorts on column header (`P` CPU%, `M` mem%, `T` time alive), live-filters with `/`, and `dd` kills with a signal picker; `+` / `-` zoom the time axis on any graph; declarative TOML layouts mean "CPU per-core full width on top, process table full width on bottom" is one config file**; pairs with [`zellij`](clis/zellij/) (run `btm` in a small dedicated pane to watch a long-running fine-tune / batch eval / training job at a glance) |
| [hyperfine](clis/hyperfine/) | Rust | MIT/Apache-2.0 (dual) | Not a model — statistically rigorous command-line benchmarking tool; runs each command N times with warmup, reports mean ± stddev plus relative-speedup ratios, detects outliers from GC pauses or disk-cache effects, auto-picks run count from observed variance | No — benchmarking harness; programmable surface is `--export-json/markdown/csv/asciidoc` for downstream charting + CI gating, plus parameter sweeps (`--parameter-scan threads 1 16`, `--parameter-list compiler gcc,clang`) for cartesian-product grids without rolling your own loop, and `--prepare` / `--cleanup` hooks for cold-cache + filesystem-reset between runs | None — sequential per-command runs (the whole point is statistical isolation); the parallelism unit is "one binary, many invocations" measured back-to-back so noise from co-tenancy is bounded | Off — no telemetry, no analytics, no phone-home; only egress is whatever the benchmarked command itself does | **The "is change A actually faster than change B" primitive — `time foo` reports one noisy sample, `hyperfine foo bar` runs each 10+ times with warmup and prints `bar ran 1.43 ± 0.04 times faster than foo` with a real confidence interval; parameter scans + JSON export turn it into the substrate for "build a perf chart for the README" or "fail CI if v2 is more than 5% slower than v1" without writing a benchmark harness**; for an LLM-CLI workflow the right `justfile` recipe is `just bench` wrapping `hyperfine --export-markdown bench.md` over the agent-touched binary, so every refactor PR includes a reproducible perf table the reviewer (human or agent) can read at a glance |
| [starship](clis/starship/) | Rust | ISC | Not a model — cross-shell prompt rendered by one static binary for bash / zsh / fish / PowerShell / Nushell / Ion / Elvish / Tcsh / Xonsh / Cmd; ~70 built-in modules detect git branch + dirty/ahead/behind, language version of the project in `pwd` for ~30 ecosystems (Rust/Go/Node/Python/Ruby/Java/.NET/Elixir/Zig/Deno/Bun…), active Kubernetes / AWS / Azure / GCP context, Nix / direnv / mise state, Docker context, battery, last-command duration + exit code | No — prompt; programmable surface is one TOML (`~/.config/starship.toml`) where every module reorders / restyles / hides via `disabled = true` or `format = ""`, plus `starship preset` for a library of starting templates; shell-side glue is one `eval "$(starship init <shell>)"` line | None — single-process render per prompt with async detection, stat-cache inside one render, and short-circuit on inapplicable modules, so a typical `<10 ms` budget holds even in monorepos with deep `.git` directories | Off — no telemetry, no analytics, no phone-home; only egress is whatever the per-language detection modules shell out to (`git`, `kubectl config current-context`, language toolchain version probes) on the local machine | **One TOML, every shell — the load-bearing claim is "your prompt no longer lies": active Kubernetes context surfaces before you `kubectl delete` in the wrong cluster, the right Python / Node / Rust version shows for the project in `pwd`, the active AWS profile is visible before `aws s3 rm`, and `starship timings` tells you which module is slow in a deep monorepo so you can disable it explicitly**; pairs with [`zoxide`](clis/zoxide/), [`atuin`](clis/atuin/), [`direnv`](clis/direnv/), and [`mise`](clis/mise/) — all init-script shell integrations that compose cleanly because none of them own the prompt and the others do not own state |
| [xq](clis/xq/) | Go | MIT | Not a model — `jq`-shaped command-line processor for **XML and HTML** built on top of `golang.org/x/net/html` + an XPath engine: pretty-prints with syntax highlighting by default, runs XPath 1.0 expressions (`-x '//book[@lang="en"]/title'`) or CSS3 selectors (`-q 'div.product > a'`), extracts attributes (`-a href`), preserves CDATA when round-tripping, and emits JSON via `-j` so the output drops straight into a `jq` pipeline | No — Unix filter; programmable surface is "stdin in, stdout out" plus the `-i` in-place mode (added in v1.4.0) for batch reformatting many XML files in a directory; composes with `curl` / `htmlq` / `jq` / `gron` / `pandoc` without glue code | None — one process per invocation; parallelism is shell pipes (`xargs -P` over a list of URLs each piped through `xq`) | Off — no telemetry, no network of its own (`xq` does not fetch URLs — that is `curl`'s job), so the threat surface is exactly the bytes you fed it on stdin | **Covers the half of the world's data that is XML or HTML**, where [`htmlq`](clis/htmlq/) covers only HTML / CSS3 and `jq` covers only JSON: Maven `pom.xml`, Spring config, SOAP responses, RSS / Atom / OPML, Android `AndroidManifest.xml`, iTunes Library, OFX bank exports, scraped web pages all become one-liners (`curl -s URL \| xq -q 'span.titleline > a' -a href` is the HN front page in one shell pipe); the `-j` flag turns "we have XML, jq downstream wants JSON" from a Python script into a single character; pairs with [`htmlq`](clis/htmlq/) (htmlq is smaller and CSS-only when XPath is overkill), [`yq`](clis/yq/) (the YAML side of the same problem space), [`jq`](clis/jq/) downstream of `xq -j`, and [`gron`](clis/gron/) when you want the document flattened to grep-able paths instead of queried |
| [gdu](clis/gdu/) | Go | MIT | Not a model — **parallel disk-usage analyzer with an interactive TUI** built on a goroutine pool sized to your CPU; full `tcell`-based TUI by default with vim-style navigation (hjkl, `d` delete with confirm, `n/s/c/M` cycle sort by name/size/items/mtime, `a` toggle apparent vs disk usage, `T` filter by file type, `t` jump to top largest files), `--non-interactive` for scripts/CI, `--archive-browsing` walks zip/jar/tar as directories, optional SQLite analyzer (added v5.33.0) for very large filesystems where in-memory traversal is too heavy | No — TUI + non-interactive scanner; programmable surface is `--non-interactive --top N` + `--show-disk-usage` + `--show-item-count` for plain-text output suitable for `awk` / `jq` / cron / Slack-webhook pipelines, plus `--ignore-dirs '/proc,/sys,...'`, `--no-cross` (do not cross mountpoints), and YAML config in `~/.gdu.yaml` for theme + style overrides | None — single-process TUI; parallelism is the file-walk goroutine pool (default = CPU count, tunable via `--max-cores`); v5.36.0 added a top-dir analyzer for non-interactive mode that drops memory consumption substantially on very large disks | Off — no telemetry, no analytics, no phone-home; only egress is the local filesystem(s) being analysed | **Genuinely fast on NVMe SSDs** — exploits SSD queue depth where `du`, `ncdu`, and even `dust` either single-thread or use much lower parallelism, so a `~/` or `/var` scan finishes in seconds where classic `du -sh *` would single-thread for minutes; the TUI is the right answer to "find what is filling the disk *and* delete it interactively" rather than running a scan, copying the path, and `rm`-ing in a separate shell; pairs with [`dust`](clis/dust/) (dust = quick one-shot bar chart, gdu = navigable + deletable), [`duf`](clis/duf/) (duf = which filesystem is full, gdu = what inside one is full), [`fclones`](clis/fclones/) + [`kondo`](clis/kondo/) (once gdu surfaces the offenders, fclones dedups and kondo wipes language-ecosystem build caches), and [`broot`](clis/broot/) (broot = fuzzy navigator with size hints, gdu = purpose-built for size triage); the `--top` mode also makes "fail nightly cron if anything in /var/log got bigger than 1 GB" a one-liner |
| [xcp](clis/xcp/) | Rust | GPL-3.0 | Not a model — **drop-in `cp` replacement** focused on speed and a real progress bar; argument shape mirrors `cp` (`-r`, `-a`, `-v`, `-f`, `-T`, `-L`) so muscle memory transfers, with extras for the modern world: `--reflink=auto/always/never` (CoW-clone instead of copy on btrfs / xfs / bcachefs / APFS — instant, 0 bytes), `--workers N` to tune the parallel I/O pool, `--gitignore` to honour `.gitignore` rules during recursive copy, `--fsync` to force durability before exit, glob-pattern source matching | No — file-copy tool; programmable surface is the flag set + exit codes; library form is `libxcp` published on crates.io (same workspace, separately versioned) for embedding the parallel copy engine in other Rust binaries | The whole point — parallel directory traversal + small-file batching + per-CPU `copy_file_range` (Linux) / `fclonefileat` (macOS APFS) fast paths; the parallelism unit is "one tree, many file-copy tasks" sized to `--workers` (default = CPU count) so on SSD-to-SSD work it is typically 2-5x `cp -r`'s wall time | Off — no telemetry, no analytics, no phone-home; only egress is the destination volume the user told it to write to | **The first `cp` with a real progress bar that does not lie** — bytes copied / total, transfer rate (`412 MB/s`), and ETA on a single status line that updates a few times per second, instead of `cp`'s silent black box; the reflink default (`--reflink=auto`) alone is install-worthy: `xcp --reflink=auto big.iso big.copy.iso` on a CoW filesystem completes in milliseconds for arbitrarily large files where plain `cp` duplicates the bytes; pairs with [`croc`](clis/croc/) (host-to-host with NAT traversal vs xcp local-or-mounted), [`rclone`](clis/rclone/) (cloud / S3 / SFTP vs xcp local FS), [`restic`](clis/restic/) (dedup'd snapshot repo vs xcp "just put a copy over there"), and [`fclones`](clis/fclones/) after the copy when the new tree may have duplicates worth reflinking; explicit AI-contributions policy in the README is a useful read for anyone shipping AI-assisted PRs to OSS infrastructure |
| [cosign](clis/cosign/) | Go | Apache-2.0 | Not a model — Sigstore CLI for signing, verifying, and storing artifacts (container images, blobs, SBOMs, in-toto attestations) with both keypair-based and **keyless** signing flows; keyless mode trades a long-lived key for a short-lived certificate issued by Fulcio against an OIDC identity (GitHub Actions, Google, Okta, Buildkite) and logs the signature in the Rekor transparency log so verification later does not need to trust the signer's key store, only their identity provider | No — single-binary CLI; programmable surface is the flag set + exit codes plus a Go SDK for embedding sign/verify in pipelines; integrates with policy engines (Kyverno, policy-controller, Connaisseur) that consume the same signature objects | Per-invocation; bulk verification is shell-loops or the `cosign verify-attestation` batched mode | Off — no analytics; signature/log entries are written to the configured Rekor instance (default public Sigstore) which is the whole point of the protocol | **Reference implementation for the supply-chain layer the container ecosystem standardised on** — `cosign sign --identity-token "$ID_TOKEN" image` + `cosign verify --certificate-identity-regexp '...' --certificate-oidc-issuer-regexp '...' image` is the canonical "prove this image came out of *that* CI job in *that* repo" handshake; pairs with [`syft`](clis/syft/) (generate the SBOM) → cosign attest (sign the SBOM as an attestation) → admission-controller verify at deploy time |
| [mycli](clis/mycli/) | Python | BSD-3-Clause | Not a model — interactive command-line client for MySQL / MariaDB / Percona built on `prompt_toolkit` with **smart auto-completion** (table names, column names, keywords, all pulled live from the connected schema and refreshed in the background), syntax highlighting, multi-line editing with proper indent, paged output, named-query favourites (`\fs name SELECT ...` then `\f name`), and a config file (`~/.myclirc`) that keeps history per-host | No — REPL; programmable surface is the SQL prompt plus `\` backslash commands borrowed from `psql` (`\dt`, `\d table`, `\l`, `\timing`, `\T markdown` to switch output style) | None — single connection per session; for parallel queries use the underlying `mysql` client or a real driver | Off — no telemetry; only egress is the database connection the user opened | **The closest thing to a desktop GUI in pure CLI form for MySQL**, sibling to [`pgcli`](clis/pgcli/) (Postgres) and [`litecli`](clis/litecli/) (SQLite) — same author, same UX, so muscle memory transfers across all three engines; the live schema-aware completion alone removes the "type `SHOW COLUMNS FROM users` to remember the column name" detour that the stock `mysql` REPL forces |
| [zola](clis/zola/) | Rust | EUPL-1.2 | Not a model — fast static-site generator distributed as one binary with no runtime dependencies: built-in Sass compilation, syntax highlighting via `syntect`, link checking, image processing (resize, format conversion), full-text search index generation (Elasticlunr), and a [Tera](https://keats.github.io/tera/) templating engine that is Jinja-shaped so Python / Django muscle memory transfers; everything is in-tree (no plugin runtime to babysit) | No — content pipeline; programmable surface is the directory layout (`content/`, `templates/`, `sass/`, `static/`) plus `config.toml` plus Tera templates; `zola serve` is the dev-loop with live reload, `zola build` is the CI command | None — single-binary build per invocation; large sites get the parallel `rayon`-based image processing pass introduced in recent releases | Off — no telemetry; no analytics, no phone-home; only egress is whatever you put in the templates | **The "drop one binary in CI and ship a site" answer** — compared to Hugo (Go, similar shape, larger plugin / theme ecosystem) and Jekyll (Ruby, requires bundler + a runtime), Zola is one statically-linked file that builds typical small-to-medium sites in well under a second; pairs cleanly with [`mdcat`](https://github.com/swsnr/mdcat) for previewing markdown locally before commit and with any static-host CDN (Netlify, Cloudflare Pages, GitHub Pages) for the deploy step |
| [bruno](clis/bruno/) | TS (Electron app + Node CLI) | MIT | Not a model — git-friendly, fully-offline API client; collections live as plain `.bru` text files in your repo, the desktop app edits them visually, and `@usebruno/cli` (`bru run`) executes one or many in CI with JUnit / JSON / HTML reporters; Jinja-style `{{var}}` interpolation pulls per-environment auth + base URLs from `.bru` env files | No — HTTP / GraphQL / WebSocket / SSE / gRPC client; programmable surface is the on-disk `.bru` DSL (method, URL, headers, body, assertions, scripts) plus `bruno.json` collection metadata, both diffable in PRs | None — single conversation per request; sandboxed JS hooks (`pre-request` / `post-response`) for HMAC / signing; concurrency is `bru run <folder>` over a directory of requests | Off — no telemetry, no account, no required network egress beyond the API the user fires at; the desktop app does not phone home, the CLI does not phone home | **Postman / Insomnia ergonomics with the cloud removed and the collection moved into git as plain text** — a PR that touches a request shows up in `git diff` exactly like a code change so reviewers read API contract changes inline, the *same* `.bru` files run in the GUI on a developer's laptop and in `bru run --reporter-junit` in CI (no two-step "export then newman"), environment files are also `.bru` so per-stage config is reviewable, and there is no hosted backplane to be on the wrong side of when it has an outage |
| [helmfile](clis/helmfile/) | Go | MIT | Not a model — declarative spec for an entire Helm release set; orchestrates `helm` (which it shells out to) plus the `helm-diff` plugin for the safety gate; environments are first-class via `{{ .Environment.Name }}` template injection over per-env values files; CNCF Sandbox project | No — Kubernetes / Helm orchestrator; programmable surface is `helmfile.yaml` (`repositories:`, `environments:`, `releases:` with cross-release `needs:` dependency graph), Go-template + Sprig for value layering, and `helmfile template` to render the whole fleet as plain manifests for ArgoCD / kustomize input | None — releases are deployed in topologically-sorted order from the `needs:` graph; siblings parallelise; `helmfile sync` is "upgrade-or-install everything idempotently"; `helmfile diff` is the dry-run gate that shells out to `helm-diff` per release | Off — no telemetry, no analytics; only egress is the `helm` chart repos you declare and the Kubernetes API server you target | **Multi-release Helm orchestration as one declarative artifact with a built-in `diff` gate** — plain `helm` solves "deploy *one* chart"; helmfile is the layer above for "install / upgrade 12 charts in a specific order across 3 namespaces with environment-specific values, then diff against the live cluster before any apply"; CI runs the same `helmfile -e prod apply` a developer ran locally against `kind`; the lighter-weight push-shaped alternative to ArgoCD / Flux for teams that want `helm` semantics in `git` rather than a controller in the cluster |
| [dyff](clis/dyff/) | Go | MIT | Not a model — structural diff tool for YAML / JSON; parses both sides as trees and emits a path-addressed list of *structural* changes (added / removed / modified / list-reordered) instead of a textual line diff | No — diff renderer; programmable surface is `--output-style json/brief` for tooling, `--filter <path>` / `--exclude <path>` for scoping, `--ignore-order-changes` for lists where order does not matter semantically, `--detect-kubernetes-entity-file` for matching multi-document streams by `kind/namespace/name` instead of stream position, `--set-exit-code` for CI gating | None — one process per pair of inputs; concurrency is shell pipes / xargs over many file pairs | Off — no telemetry, no network; pure local file diff | **The viewer that makes `helm template`, `kustomize build`, `kubectl diff`, and `kubectl apply --dry-run=server -o yaml` actually reviewable** — a `yq -i 'sort_keys(..)'` run that shows up as a full-file rewrite in `git diff` reduces to "no semantic changes, only key ordering" in `dyff`; a renamed key 200 lines down is recognised as the same key by structural path, not invented as two unrelated edits; `dyff between live.yaml proposed.yaml --filter spec.template` only reports changes under one subtree, the right tool for diffing a giant rendered manifest where you only care about the deployment spec and not the autogenerated revision-annotation churn |
| [htmlq](clis/htmlq/) | Rust | MIT | Not a model — `jq`-shaped Unix filter for HTML built on the `html5ever` parser (the same engine that powers Servo / Firefox's experimental Quantum work) so it eats real-world soup (unclosed tags, three different encoding declarations, malformed `<!DOCTYPE>`) without choking; full CSS3 selectors (`div.product > a.title`, `a[href^="https://"]`, `tr:nth-child(odd) td:last-of-type`); output flags include `--text` (visible text only), `--attribute href` (extract one attribute, the killer combo for link harvesting), `--pretty` (reflow), `--base URL` (resolve relative links), `--remove-nodes 'selector'` (delete chrome before piping onward) | No — Unix filter; programmable surface is "stdin in, stdout out" so it composes with `curl` / [`strip-tags`](clis/strip-tags/) / [`jq`](clis/jq/) / [`pandoc`](https://pandoc.org) / [`mdcat`](https://github.com/swsnr/mdcat) without glue code | None — one process per invocation; parallelism is shell pipes (`xargs -P` over a list of URLs, each piped through `htmlq`) | Off — no telemetry, no network of its own (`htmlq` does *not* fetch URLs — that is `curl` / `wget`'s job), so the threat surface is exactly the HTML you fed it on stdin | **The structured-extraction layer for `curl`-then-grep pipelines — `curl -s URL \| htmlq -a href 'a.story'` is a one-liner where the Python `requests + bs4` equivalent is a script; pairs with [`strip-tags`](clis/strip-tags/) (htmlq narrows to the right region, strip-tags drops the rest of the chrome before an LLM prompt) and with [`jq`](clis/jq/) / [`jaq`](clis/jaq/) when the page embeds JSON-LD inside `<script type="application/ld+json">`**; cannot execute JavaScript so client-side-rendered pages need Playwright / `chromium-headless --dump-dom` first; project quiet since the v0.4.0 tag (early 2022) but still works because `html5ever` and the CSS-selector crates have stayed stable — treat as a battle-tested classic, not an active roadmap |

Latest additions: [`mc`](clis/mc/) (4.8.33, GPL-3.0-or-later) — MidnightCommander/mc's venerable two-pane Norton-Commander-style terminal file manager that has shipped in every Linux distro for three decades and is still actively maintained: function-key hints across the bottom row (`F3` view, `F4` edit, `F5` copy, `F6` move, `F8` delete, `F9` menus), built-in `mcedit` text + hex viewers, transparent VFS so `cd` into a `.tar.gz` / `.zip` / `.iso` / SFTP URL (`cd sh://user@host/path`) / FTP URL works as a regular directory, per-directory user-menu (`F2`) shell scriptlets the whole team triggers from one keystroke, and a real subshell under the panels (`Ctrl+O` toggles, `Ctrl+Enter` pastes the highlighted filename onto the command line) — the on-ramp every shell newcomer learns first and still the right answer for triage on a fresh server where the only installed thing is the distro default toolset; [`markdownlint-cli2`](clis/markdownlint-cli2/) (v0.22.1, MIT) — DavidAnson/markdownlint-cli2's fast configuration-file-driven CLI front-end to the `markdownlint` library that powers VS Code's "markdownlint" extension and ships ~50 built-in rules covering heading hierarchy / list consistency / trailing whitespace + line length / code-fence style / broken or inconsistent links / HTML usage in Markdown, with `.markdownlint-cli2.jsonc` / `.yaml` / `.cjs` config so rule selection, glob includes / excludes, and custom rules live next to the source, `--fix` for the deterministic-fix tail, first-class `.gitignore` honouring (`gitignore: true`) so CI runs match local dev, and a GitHub Action + `pre-commit` hook + Docker image + the same VS Code extension all using *one* engine so editor diagnostics and CI gate cannot drift — the maintained successor to the older `markdownlint-cli` (which is in maintenance), pairs with [`prettier`](https://prettier.io) (formatting markdownlint does not do) and [`vale`](https://vale.sh) (prose style, different layer); [`dotenvx`](clis/dotenvx/) (v1.64.0, BSD-3-Clause) — dotenvx/dotenvx's secure modern successor to the original `dotenv` (by the same author) that makes a `.env` file safe to commit by *encrypting* the values with a public key while the matching private key lives in `.env.keys` outside git, with `dotenvx run -- node index.js` (or `python app.py`, or `cargo run`, or any other process) loading + decrypting + injecting envs at exec time so application code drops the `require('dotenv').config()` line entirely, multi-environment overlays (`.env.production` + per-env encrypted overlays + explicit precedence rules), `--overload` / `--no-override` semantics, and a single static binary built with Bun / pkg for every major OS / arch (no Node runtime required) — the right shape for a polyglot repo where one secret-handling story across Node + Python + Rust + shell beats one `dotenv`-clone per language and where the deployment target (small VPS / Render / Fly / docker image) does not justify a full secret-manager round trip. Latest additions: [`xq`](clis/xq/) (v1.4.0, MIT) — sibprogrammer/xq's Go-implemented `jq`-shaped processor for **XML and HTML** (the half of the world's data `jq` does not touch): pretty-print + syntax-highlight by default, XPath 1.0 (`-x '//book/title'`) or CSS3 (`-q 'a.story'`) for extraction, attribute pull (`-a href`), `-j` to emit JSON so a `jq` pipeline takes over, `-i` for batch in-place reformatting (added v1.4.0); `curl -s URL | xq -q 'span.titleline > a' -a href` is the HN front page in one shell pipe and the Python `requests + lxml` equivalent is a script; [`gdu`](clis/gdu/) (v5.36.0, MIT) — dundee/gdu's Go-implemented **parallel disk-usage analyzer** with a vim-keybind TUI that finishes a `~/` scan in seconds where `du -sh *` would single-thread for minutes (goroutine pool sized to CPU exploits NVMe queue depth), `--non-interactive --top N` for cron / Slack-webhook reports, `--archive-browsing` walks zip / jar / tar as directories, optional SQLite analyzer for huge filesystems where in-memory traversal is too heavy, `d` deletes interactively with a confirmation popup defaulting to "no"; [`xcp`](clis/xcp/) (v0.24.7, GPL-3.0) — tarka/xcp's Rust **drop-in `cp` replacement** with a real progress bar (bytes / rate / ETA on one status line that updates a few times per second), parallel directory walk + small-file batching for 2-5x `cp -r` wall time on SSDs, `--reflink=auto` CoW-clones on btrfs / xfs / bcachefs / APFS so `xcp --reflink=auto big.iso big.copy.iso` completes in milliseconds for arbitrarily large files instead of duplicating bytes, `--gitignore` honours `.gitignore` during recursive copy so `node_modules` / `target` / virtualenvs do not bloat the destination tree.

Recent additions: [`bacon`](clis/bacon/) (v3.22.0, AGPL-3.0) — Canop/bacon's background Rust code-checker that watches the file tree and re-runs `cargo check` / `clippy` / `test` / `nextest` / `doc` on every save, distilling the result into a single-screen view (warnings collapsed by default, errors expanded with file:line links) and hot-swapping between jobs with `c` / `w` / `t` / `d` keystrokes — sits in a small `tmux` / `zellij` pane next to the editor so the "save → 8 s `cargo check` round-trip" loop becomes a glance instead of a context switch, with per-project `bacon.toml` declaring custom jobs (`cross check`, `cargo +nightly clippy`, scoped `nextest` runs) and on-success hooks; [`git-cliff`](clis/git-cliff/) (v2.13.1, Apache-2.0) — orhun/git-cliff's Conventional-Commits-aware changelog generator that walks `git log` between two refs, parses commit messages against a configurable regex grammar in `cliff.toml`, groups commits by type (feat / fix / docs / perf / breaking) ordered by precedence, and renders the result through a Tera template with presets for Keep-a-Changelog / GitHub releases / GitLab / Gitea / Cocogitto — `git cliff --unreleased` previews the next release notes, `git cliff --bump` auto-detects the next semver from breaking-change footers + commit types, and `git cliff --tag v2.0.0 --output CHANGELOG.md` cuts a dated section into the file in one command, the practical answer to "what semver is this and what changed" without standing up `release-please` / `semantic-release`; [`mprocs`](clis/mprocs/) (v0.9.2, MIT) — pvolok/mprocs's two-pane TUI runner for multiple long-lived shell processes (process list on the left, focused process's combined stdout+stderr scrollback with ANSI colour preserved on the right) declared as `mprocs.yaml` with per-process `cmd` / `cwd` / `env` / `autostart` / `autorestart` / `stop` (signal or literal keystrokes) — the dedicated answer to "five terminals: `pnpm dev`, `cargo run`, `docker compose up postgres redis`, `wrangler tail`, `pytest --watch`" without learning `tmux` and without `foreman`'s interleaved-stream readability collapse, with graceful per-process shutdown on `q` so the local Postgres container actually stops instead of leaking; the layer-pair to [`zellij`](clis/zellij/) (zellij multiplexes terminals, mprocs multiplexes processes inside one).

Earlier additions: [`just`](clis/just/) (1.50.0, CC0-1.0) — casey/just's Rust-implemented project-local command runner where the `make` syntax pain is gone (tabs-only, `$$`-to-escape-`$`, shell-per-line resets cwd, implicit rules firing when you didn't ask) and what survives is a small DSL with real argument passing (`just deploy production` vs `just deploy` defaulting to `staging`), per-recipe shebangs (one recipe can be a Python script, the next a `bash -eu` block, the next a `nu` snippet — no `bash -c heredoc` gymnastics), `--list` auto-help from doc comments, `--choose` fzf-picker over recipes, dotenv loading via `set dotenv-load := true`, and OS-conditional `[macos]` / `[linux]` / `[windows]` recipe attributes — for an LLM-CLI workflow `justfile` is the right place to formalise the agent-callable surface (`just lint`, `just test`, `just typecheck`, `just fmt-check`) so a `CLAUDE.md` / `AGENTS.md` reference stays stable when the underlying tool swaps from `cargo` to `bazel` or `npm` to `pnpm`; [`tokei`](clis/tokei/) (v14.0.0, MIT/Apache-2.0) — XAMPPRocky's Rust rewrite of `cloc` with per-language tokenizer state machines (string-aware, nested-comment-aware) for ~250 languages including modern syntax (Rust raw strings, Swift multi-line literals, Vue / Svelte / MDX SFCs, TSX, Nix, Zig, Gleam) where regex-based counters miscount, `rayon`-parallel tree walk so a 1M-LOC repo finishes in well under a second, first-class machine output (`--output json/yaml/cbor/openmetrics` — the OpenMetrics exporter drops straight into Prometheus pushgateway), and `--files` per-file mode for `jq` post-processing — `tokei -t Rust --files -o json` is the cheapest way to feed an agent the shape of a codebase before asking it to plan refactors, dropping into a context packer ([`files-to-prompt`](clis/files-to-prompt/), [`code2prompt`](clis/code2prompt/), [`repomix`](clis/repomix/)) as a budget hint; [`gum`](clis/gum/) (v0.17.0, MIT) — charmbracelet's Go-implemented TUI widget set exposed as standalone shell commands (`gum input` / `choose` / `confirm` / `spin` / `filter` / `table` / `write` / `format` / `style` / `file` / `pager`) where every widget reads from stdin / argv and writes to stdout so they compose with shell pipes the way Unix commands always have, theme inheritance via `GUM_*` env vars sourced from `.zshrc` keeps the Charm look consistent across every script in a repo, no language lock-in (calls work identically from bash / zsh / fish / nu / PowerShell / Makefiles / justfiles / Python `subprocess`) — for an LLM-CLI workflow turns the human-in-the-loop confirmation step from a janky `read -r REPLY` into a real picker: `gum choose` the model, `gum input --password` the API key, `gum confirm` the destructive action, `gum spin --title "thinking..." --` around the agent invocation, five lines of shell, looks like a product.

Earlier additions: [`lazydocker`](clis/lazydocker/) (v0.25.2, MIT) — jesseduffield's five-panel Docker / Compose TUI where containers, images, volumes, networks, and stack services each get a panel and every routine ops verb (logs, exec, restart, rebuild, prune) is one or two keystrokes against the highlighted row, with live `docker stats`-shaped CPU / memory / network sparklines per container so "which one is melting" is a glance not a script; [`jless`](clis/jless/) (v0.9.0, MIT) — PaulJuliusMartinez's vim-style JSON / YAML pager (`hjkl` / `f` / `t` / fold / `:N` jump) that streams documents as a navigable tree without loading the whole file as a single Python / `jq` value, the right tool for an `aws ec2 describe-instances` blob or a 200 MB CDK synth output you want to *read*, not transform; [`duf`](clis/duf/) (v0.9.1, MIT) — muesli's friendlier `df` that groups mounted filesystems by category (local / network / fuse / special) with colour-coded usage bars, sortable columns, `--json` for monitoring scripts, and `--only` / `--hide` filters so the question "which of my real disks is full" goes from "scan 30 lines of `df -h`" to "look at the one row whose bar is red". Earlier additions: [`zellij`](clis/zellij/) (v0.44.1, MIT) — zellij-org's Rust-implemented terminal multiplexer where the `tmux`-onboarding-cliff is filed off: visible status + tab bar by default, the bottom strip lists the keys for the current mode so workflows are discoverable not memorized, `Ctrl+G` lock-mode passes every key through to the inner program for editor-keymap conflicts, layouts are KDL files (declarative, diffable in git, one-command boot of multi-pane workspaces), floating panes toggle with one keystroke, and the WebAssembly plugin runtime makes third-party widgets (richer status bars, keybind helpers, fullscreen-with-search) drop in as one `*.wasm` file under `~/.config/zellij/plugins/` — for an LLM-CLI workflow that wants "editor in pane 1, REPL in pane 2, agent log tail in pane 3, git status in pane 4" as one command, collapses setup from "five `tmux send-keys` calls" to one `zellij --layout llm-dev`;
