[`yazi`](clis/yazi/) (v26.1.22, MIT) — sxyazi's async-first Rust file manager with a `ranger`-style three-column TUI where every filesystem operation runs on a Tokio runtime so cursoring onto a 100k-entry directory or a slow network mount never freezes the UI (loading state + update-when-ready instead of block-the-event-loop), inline image previews via the terminal's native graphics protocol with no `ueberzug` daemon, bulk-rename through `$EDITOR` (select with `space`, hit `:` rename, edit the names in vim, save, yazi applies the diff), and a Lua plugin runtime + on-disk keybind / opener DSL so customization is a config file not a recompile — pairs with the shell wrapper that `cd`s the parent shell to wherever yazi exited for a one-keystroke "navigate visually, drop back to the right shell prompt" flow; [`bottom`](clis/bottom/) (0.12.3, MIT) — ClementTsang's cross-platform graphical system monitor (`btm`) where CPU per-core / memory / swap / network / temperature / disk IO / battery render as braille-character sparklines (the curve answers "is this spike a runaway, a workload, or a brief blip" before you have to think about it), runs natively on Windows where `htop` does not with the same keybinds across all platforms, process table sorts on column header and live-filters with `/`, `dd` kills with a signal picker, and the dashboard layout is a TOML file declaring a tree of widgets so "CPU per-core full width on top, process table full width on bottom" is one config swap — runs in a small `zellij` / `tmux` pane to watch a long-running fine-tune or batch eval at a glance.

Earlier additions: [`lazygit`](clis/lazygit/) (v0.61.1, MIT) — jesseduffield's Go-implemented five-panel git TUI (status / files / branches / commits / stash) where every common git operation is one or two keystrokes: per-hunk + per-line staging without `git add -p`'s modal prompts, interactive rebase as a live editable TUI (`s` squash, `f` fixup, `d` drop, `Ctrl+J/K` reorder), three-way conflict resolution with picker UI instead of conflict markers, custom-commands YAML DSL for project-specific keybinds, and `o` on a branch shells out to `gh pr create` if `gh` is on `$PATH` — for an LLM-CLI workflow that produces frequent small commits that need squashing / reordering / amending before push, collapses the "clean up the history before push" step from minutes to seconds; [`delta`](clis/delta/) (0.19.2, MIT) — dandavison's `syntect`-backed diff pager you wire into `core.pager` once and never think about again: side-by-side layout for long moved blocks (a 50-line function moved between files becomes readable instead of a wall of `-` followed by a wall of `+`), real per-language syntax highlighting on each `+` / `-` line (Rust lifetimes, Python f-strings, TSX, Markdown all colored correctly via Sublime `.tmTheme` files), three-way merge conflict rendering (ours / base / theirs in three columns instead of `<<<<<<<` markers in your editor), and `delta.navigate = true` adds `n` / `N` keybinds to jump between hunks — pairs with [`lazygit`](clis/lazygit/) automatically when both are wired into the same `~/.gitconfig`; [`jj`](clis/jj/) (v0.40.0, Apache-2.0) — jj-vcs's git-compatible VCS that fixes git's commit model: every working-tree edit is automatically a commit (no `add` / `commit` cycle), the operation log (`jj op log`) records every repo-modifying operation and `jj op restore <op-id>` rolls the entire repo back to that operation's state including working copy + bookmarks (the universal undo), conflicts are first-class commit content (a `jj rebase` over a conflicting change *succeeds* — the resulting "conflicted commit" can be rebased / split / abandoned without resolving first), and change IDs (stable across rewrites) are separate from commit IDs (which change on every rewrite) so `jj rebase` / `jj squash` / `jj split` don't break references — `jj git init --colocate` mode means a `jj`-managed repo is also a normal git repo every teammate can use with plain `git`, so adoption is per-individual not per-team. Earlier additions: [`posting`](clis/posting/) (v2.10.0, Apache-2.0) — darrenburns's Textual-TUI HTTP / REST / GraphQL client, the keyboard-first Postman / Insomnia replacement that lives inside `tmux` / SSH (`Ctrl+J` send, `Ctrl+P` command palette, `Ctrl+S` save) and stores collections as plain YAML in git instead of a vendor sync product, with `{{VAR}}` interpolation pulling auth + base URLs from `.env` + typed `*.env.yaml` overlays so the same request fires correctly against staging / prod without copying secrets into the body; [`tach`](clis/tach/) (v0.34.1, MIT) — gauge-sh's Rust-fast Python module-dependency linter, the "import-linter that you actually adopt" (`tach mod` lists modules, `tach sync` infers the current dependency edges as the baseline, `tach check` fails CI on undeclared imports) so a growing Python codebase gets the layered-architecture hygiene Java / Go / Rust have by default — the PyO3-bound Rust core parses tens of thousands of files per second so the check is cheap on every PR, `tach show --format mermaid` exports the graph for docs, and `tach test --base origin/main` runs only the tests downstream of the diff (the Python answer to `bazel query`); [`oxc`](clis/oxc/) (apps_v1.61.0, MIT) — oxc-project's Rust-rewrite-of-the-JS-toolchain umbrella, with `oxlint` as the flagship: a near-drop-in `eslint` replacement that runs 50–100× faster (~500 ported rules across `import` / `jsdoc` / `jest` / `react` / `react-hooks` / `typescript` / `unicorn` / `jsx-a11y` / `n` / `oxc` / `vitest` / `promise` plugins), can be run *alongside* `eslint` for the unported tail, and the broader `oxc_*` crate set (parser / semantic / resolver / formatter / minifier / transformer) is the building blocks for downstream Rust-native bundlers (Rolldown, Rspack, Tsdown, Rstest, the Void Zero stack) — the JS / TS counterpart to what `ruff` did for Python and `uv` did for `pip`. Earlier additions: [`prefect`](clis/prefect/) (v3.6.28, Apache-2.0) — PrefectHQ's Python-native workflow orchestrator, the decorator-shaped peer to [`dagster`](clis/dagster/) for AI / data pipelines that don't justify Airflow (`@flow` / `@task` decorators, retries / caching / concurrency as kwargs not YAML, local SQLite → managed Postgres upgrade is a connection-string swap, v3.x replaced `agent` with pull-based `worker` pools); [`harlequin`](clis/harlequin/) (v2.5.2, MIT) — tconbeer's Textual SQL IDE for the terminal, the missing real SQL editor inside `tmux` / SSH (lazy-loaded schema tree + multi-buffer SQL editor with live-catalog autocomplete + arrow-key navigable results grid against DuckDB / Postgres / MySQL / SQLite / Snowflake / BigQuery / Trino / MotherDuck / ODBC from one binary), the interactive operator-side counterpart to [`datasette`](clis/datasette/) and [`sqlite-utils`](clis/sqlite-utils/); [`sqlite-utils`](clis/sqlite-utils/) (v3.39, Apache-2.0) — Simon Willison's SQLite Swiss-army CLI, the shortest path from "I have a file" to "I have a queryable database" (`sqlite-utils insert mydata.db events events.csv --csv --detect-types` creates the table, infers column types, and bulk-inserts in one call; `sqlite-utils memory access.csv "select status, count(*) from t group by 1"` runs SQL against a CSV without ever materializing a file), the upstream loader / schema-mutator that produces the `.db` other tools open. Earlier additions: [`dlt`](clis/dlt/) (v1.25.0, Apache-2.0) — dlt-hub's "data load tool", a `pip install`-shaped Python library that turns a `@dlt.resource` generator into a schema-evolving, incremental, transactional EL pipeline against any of ~20 destinations (DuckDB / Postgres / BigQuery / Snowflake / Redshift / Databricks / MotherDuck / ClickHouse / Synapse / Athena / filesystem-parquet on S3 / GCS / Azure) **including the vector-store destinations LanceDB / Qdrant / Weaviate**, so 20 lines replace a Singer tap or an Airbyte connector for landing a third-party API into a warehouse or a RAG index, with nested arrays normalising into typed child tables, watermarks persisting in `_dlt_pipeline_state`, and the same pipeline running locally (`destination="duckdb"`), in CI (`filesystem`), and in prod (`snowflake`) by changing one argument; [`verba`](clis/verba/) (v2.1.3, BSD-3-Clause) — Weaviate's "Golden RAGtriever", a typed-component RAG application (Reader → Chunker → Embedder → Retriever → Generator, every stage a swappable Pydantic class registered on import) with a bundled React UI in front of [`weaviate`](clis/weaviate/) and OpenAI / Anthropic / Cohere / Ollama / SentenceTransformers selectable per-stage in the Settings panel, the permissive choice in the self-hostable RAG niche where peers like [`khoj`](clis/khoj/) and [`firecrawl`](clis/firecrawl/) are AGPL-3.0; [`autoevals`](clis/autoevals/) (py-0.2.0, MIT) — Braintrust's small MIT scoring library packaging the standard set of LLM scoring functions (`Factuality`, `AnswerRelevancy`, `AnswerCorrectness`, `Battle`, `ClosedQA`, `Possible`, `Security`, `Sql`, `Translation`, `LLMClassifier` builder over Chevron prompts, plus heuristic `Levenshtein` / `JSONDiff` / `EmbeddingSimilarity`) as plain callables with a uniform `(input?, output, expected?, **kwargs) -> Score` signature in Python *and* TypeScript at parity, the layer underneath the gating-shaped harnesses ([`promptfoo`](clis/promptfoo/), [`deepeval`](clis/deepeval/)) that wrap a copy of these scorers anyway — drop into pytest / a notebook / a CI step / a custom eval loop without adopting a project shape; [`tinygrad`](clis/tinygrad/) (v0.12.0, MIT) — a small, hackable PyTorch-shaped DL framework whose entire pipeline (frontend → UOp IR → scheduler → backend code-gen for CUDA / HIP / Metal / WebGPU / OpenCL / CPU) fits in ~10k lines of readable Python, with a beam-search autotuner (`BEAM=2`), `DEBUG=4` to print generated backend source, native multi-device sharding, and reference LLaMA-3 / SDXL / Whisper inference scripts under `examples/`; the catalog's only entry where "fork the framework" is a sensible answer to a feature gap and the production path for AMD ROCm / Apple Metal / WebGPU inference where the PyTorch backend story is rough; [`candle`](clis/candle/) (v0.10.1, Apache-2.0 OR MIT dual) — Hugging Face's minimalist Rust ML framework with `safetensors` + native GGUF support, reference impls of every architecture the HF Hub cares about (LLaMA / Mistral / Qwen / Phi / Gemma / DeepSeek / Whisper / SD / SDXL / Flux), and the CUDA / Metal / CPU backends needed to compile a single static binary that runs production inference with no Python runtime — the right answer for Tauri desktop, edge, Lambda cold-start, or browser-via-WASM deploys, with Apple Silicon Metal acceleration first-class and the production HTTP-serving layer (paged-attention + continuous batching + dynamic LoRA) sitting downstream as `mistral.rs`; [`guidellm`](clis/guidellm/) (v0.6.0, Apache-2.0) — vllm-project's load-generation and benchmarking CLI for LLM inference servers whose `--rate-type sweep` mode auto-walks the request-rate axis from 1 → throughput-saturation in one command and emits the full latency-vs-throughput Pareto curve as console + HTML + JSON, with token-aware request shaping (uses the model's *real* tokenizer to construct prompts at the requested input-token count, not character count) so the numbers survive the deploy; the catalog's reference for "how fast / how cheap is my LLM serving stack under realistic load?" before picking a GPU SKU, comparing vLLM-vs-SGLang-vs-Q4-vs-FP8 apples-to-apples, or sizing per-token economics against a hosted-API alternative; [`trl`](clis/trl/) (v1.3.0, Apache-2.0) — Hugging Face's RL + post-training library, the canonical home of `SFTTrainer` / `DPOTrainer` / `GRPOTrainer` / `PPOTrainer` / `RewardTrainer` and the reference implementation of every preference-optimisation paper (DPO / IPO / KTO / ORPO / SimPO / BCO / CPO / Online-DPO / RLOO / GRPO) downstream wrappers (Unsloth, Axolotl, Llama-Factory, alignment-handbook) compose against; `GRPOTrainer(reward_funcs=[...])` makes RLVR-style reasoning RL a 50-line script with built-in vLLM rollout integration, and multimodal SFT + DPO are in-tree on the same surface; [`peft`](clis/peft/) (v0.19.1, Apache-2.0) — Hugging Face's parameter-efficient fine-tuning library, the canonical implementation of LoRA / QLoRA / DoRA / VeRA / IA3 / OFT / BOFT / LoHa / LoKr / X-LoRA / FourierFT / VBLoRA / RandLoRA / Prompt-Tuning / P-Tuning / Prefix-Tuning whose `safetensors` adapter format is the de-facto standard every multi-LoRA serving engine (`vllm --enable-lora`, [`lorax`](clis/lorax/), [`text-generation-inference`](clis/text-generation-inference/) multi-LoRA) consumes, with runtime adapter swap (`model.set_adapter("customer_x")`) as the killer feature for multi-tenant SaaS; [`lerobot`](clis/lerobot/) (v0.5.1, Apache-2.0) — Hugging Face's end-to-end robot-learning stack with datasets, pretrained VLA policies (ACT, Diffusion Policy, π0, π0-fast, SmolVLA, VQ-BeT, TD-MPC2, SAC), Mujoco-based sim envs, and hardware drivers (SO-100 / SO-101, Koch, ALOHA, Stretch, Trossen, Unitree) sharing one `Robot` / `Teleop` / `Policy` ABC, with the SO-100 open-source ~$200 arm making the real-hardware on-ramp a weekend project; [`fast-graphrag`](clis/fast-graphrag/) (HEAD-pinned, MIT) — circlemind's small, readable GraphRAG library that does typed `instructor`-driven entity / relation extraction and answers via personalised-PageRank traversal across the entity graph, with local pickled stores + `igraph` and OpenAI-compatible swappability for the LLM and embedding clients, the catalog's reference for "GraphRAG, on this laptop, by Friday" without standing up Neo4j; [`deer-flow`](clis/deer-flow/) (HEAD-pinned, MIT) — ByteDance's LangGraph-shaped long-horizon SuperAgent harness with role-specialised planner / researcher / coder / reporter / background-investigator subagents, sandboxed tool-use, shared memory, human-in-the-loop interrupts, and a graph-level time-travel debugger, the first open release that ships the full multi-agent deep-research split most demos approximate; [`anything-llm`](clis/anything-llm/) (v1.12.1, MIT) — Mintplex Labs' batteries-included self-hostable RAG / agent platform with multi-source ingestion (PDF / URL / GitHub / Confluence / Notion), per-workspace LLM + vector-store + embedder selection, agent + MCP tool-use, and chat-widget / Chrome / desktop / API distribution surfaces; [`dagster`](clis/dagster/) (1.13.2, Apache-2.0) — software-defined-asset orchestration platform whose typed asset graph + partitioned backfills + code-versioned memoisation absorb the growth from "a notebook calling OpenAI in a loop on a cron" into a real LLM-pipeline runtime, with `dagster-openai` / `dagster-anthropic` / `dagster-pinecone` / `dagster-weaviate` resources wiring the model and vector-store tiers in; [`milvus`](clis/milvus/) (v2.6.15, Apache-2.0) — high-performance Go + C++ vector database with DiskANN + GPU-CAGRA index families and first-class hybrid dense + sparse + scalar retrieval, the catalog's reference vector store for past-50M-vector RAG corpora on Kubernetes where single-binary peers ([`qdrant`](clis/qdrant/), [`weaviate`](clis/weaviate/)) start to strain; [`docsgpt`](clis/docsgpt/) (v0.17.0, MIT) — self-hostable RAG agent platform with a no-code agent builder, multi-source ingestion (Confluence / Notion / GitHub / Drive / S3 / web crawl), MCP tool mounts, and ready-made Chrome / Discord / Chatwoot bridges for non-technical end-users; [`huggingface_hub`](clis/huggingface_hub/) (v1.11.0, Apache-2.0) — the official Python client + `hf` CLI for the Hugging Face Hub, the universal weight-transport layer every other entry in the catalog touches (download / upload / cache + the `InferenceClient` that routes hosted-LLM calls across Together / Replicate / Fal / SambaNova / Cerebras / Nebius / Groq via `provider="auto"`), with the new `hf jobs run` subcommand submitting Docker-shaped jobs to hosted GPU infra and `tiny-agents` showing the `MCPClient` + `InferenceClient` ReAct pattern in <100 lines; [`gradio`](clis/gradio/) (v6.13.0, Apache-2.0) — the *default* demo-UI primitive of the open-weight model ecosystem: one Python function becomes a typed web UI + streaming HTTP API with OpenAPI docs + Python / JS client SDK + an MCP server (via `mcp_server=True`) + a public `gradio.live` share URL in one `launch()` call, with first-class multimodal components (`Image` / `Audio` / `Video` / `Dataframe` / `Model3D`) and a `gradio_client` package that turns any deployed Space into a remote-callable Python function; [`cog`](clis/cog/) (v0.18.0, Apache-2.0) — Replicate's opinionated container builder for ML models: `cog.yaml` declares Python / CUDA / system packages + a typed `Predictor.predict(...)` entry-point and `cog build` produces a reproducible GPU container with a generated FastAPI server, OpenAPI schema, and a curated CUDA / cuDNN / Torch matrix selected automatically, the same image running locally with `cog predict` and on hosted infra after `cog push r8.im/owner/model` — Dockerfile-free GPU packaging for single-model APIs; [`datachain`](clis/datachain/) (v0.54.0, Apache-2.0) — datachain-ai's pandas / polars-shaped Python library + CLI for building, versioning, and querying multimodal **unstructured-data datasets** (images / video / audio / PDFs / text) against a SQLite (or Postgres / ClickHouse) catalog while the bytes stay in S3 / GCS / Azure / local FS by content-addressed manifest, so a 10 TB image corpus enriched with CLIP embeddings + GPT-4o captions versions in seconds without copying bytes; UDFs declare input columns with type hints, Pydantic models become row schemas, and a `Chain` of `gen` / `map` / `filter` / `agg` / `save` operators compiles to one query plan with checkpoint-and-resume so an enrichment pass survives an OOM mid-run — the headless / SQL-shaped data-engineering counterpart to [`fiftyone`](clis/fiftyone/)'s App-in-the-loop visual-AI workflow and the [`dvc`](https://dvc.org) peer for the LLM-annotation era; [`trackio`](clis/trackio/) (trackio@0.25.1, MIT) — Hugging Face's lightweight, local-first experiment tracker that ships as a `wandb`-API-compatible drop-in (`import trackio as wandb`) so an existing fine-tuning script (HF `Trainer`, `accelerate`, `lightning`, plain `torch`) flips from a SaaS-billed dashboard to a local SQLite log without touching any `wandb.log` call, with a Gradio dashboard at `trackio show`, opt-in one-line mirror to a free Hugging Face Space (`space_id="user/run"`), and `import_csv` / `import_tfevents` backfill from existing logs — the "I just want to plot a loss curve and not get billed" tier underneath heavier trackers like [`mlflow`](clis/mlflow/) / [`aim`](clis/aim/); [`fiftyone`](clis/fiftyone/) (v1.14.2, Apache-2.0) — voxel51's dataset / visual-AI workbench: typed `Sample` collection (image + detections + segmentations + classifications + arbitrary fields) with an Electron + browser App that renders a sample grid, per-sample modal view with predictions overlaid on pixels, embeddings projector (`fob.compute_visualization` → UMAP / t-SNE), and similarity search backed by a configurable vector index (sklearn / Qdrant / Pinecone / LanceDB / Milvus / Redis / MongoDB Atlas Vector Search), plus the Brain layer (`uniqueness`, `mistakenness`, `hardness`, `representativeness`, `near_duplicates`) that turns "what's wrong with my dataset" into one-line method calls — the dataset-side counterpart to [`promptfoo`](clis/promptfoo/) / [`deepeval`](clis/deepeval/) eval harnesses (they score outputs; fiftyone makes the inputs and labels queryable as a typed collection), with a v1 release that stabilised the Python SDK + REST API enough that an agent CLI can drive it as a long-running tool; [`lance`](clis/lance/) (v4.0.1, Apache-2.0) — lance-format/lance's open lakehouse format for multimodal AI: a Rust core with Python (`pip install pylance`) / Java / JS bindings that converts Parquet / Arrow / Pandas / Polars / DuckDB tables to a `.lance` directory in two lines and gives O(1) random row access, IVF-PQ + HNSW vector indexes, full-text search, and zero-copy versioning over the same files on local FS / S3 / GCS / Azure Blob / R2 with no daemon — your training data, retrieval index, and evaluation snapshots all live as the same versioned directory you `aws s3 sync` or check into a data lake, and the [`lancedb`](https://github.com/lancedb/lancedb) sister project adds an embedded vector-DB layer on top when you want a queryable store rather than a raw format; [`vespa`](clis/vespa/) (v8.677.31, Apache-2.0) — vespa-engine/vespa's distributed serving platform (Yahoo's open-sourced search backbone), the rare engine that combines structured search + vector ANN (HNSW) + full-text (BM25 / nativeRank) + per-query ML inference (ONNX / XGBoost / TF) inside one ranking expression evaluated server-side, so a hybrid retrieval with a learned cross-encoder re-rank lives in one round-trip and one tail-latency budget instead of three services — `brew install vespa-cli` + `vespa deploy <app-pkg>` ships a directory of XML schema + ONNX models against `docker run vespaengine/vespa` (single-node dev) or a self-hosted JVM cluster (separate config / content / container nodes) or Vespa Cloud with the same subcommands, the heavyweight production answer where [`qdrant`](clis/qdrant/) / [`weaviate`](clis/weaviate/) / [`milvus`](clis/milvus/) hand off when "we want a learned re-ranker, server-side, under a strict SLO" becomes the requirement; [`weaviate-cli`](clis/weaviate-cli/) (v3.4.0, BSD-3-Clause) — weaviate/weaviate-cli's official Python-packaged operator surface for an existing Weaviate instance: `pip install weaviate-cli` ships one `weaviate` binary that does schema CRUD, bulk import, backup / restore, tenant management, and ad-hoc query (`weaviate collection create | list | delete`, `weaviate tenant create`, `weaviate data import`, `weaviate query near-text`, `weaviate backup create`) against a local Docker dev box and a managed Weaviate Cloud cluster with the same `WCD_URL` / `WCD_API_KEY` env vars, stable exit codes + `--output json` everywhere making it trivially CI-able for the "create a collection, push a JSONL dump, snapshot, swap into prod, fail back if recall drops" loop where the language clients are the wrong tool.

Latest additions: [`fnm`](clis/fnm/) (v1.39.0, GPL-3.0) — Schniz/fnm's Rust-implemented Fast Node Manager: same per-shell `.node-version` / `.nvmrc` auto-switching as `nvm` but as a single static binary plus a 50-line `eval "$(fnm env --use-on-cd)"` shim, so the `~/.zshrc` startup tax drops from ~600 ms to tens of ms and `cd` into a project root swaps Node versions in well under 100 ms; first-class Windows support via winget, deterministic checksum-verified tarball installs under `~/.local/share/fnm/`, per-shell ephemeral `PATH` so two terminal tabs can run different Node versions concurrently — pairs with [`mise`](clis/mise/) (use `mise` when you need Node + Python + Go + Ruby in one tool, `fnm` when Node is the only language to multi-version) and [`volta`](clis/volta/) (Volta pins toolchain versions inside `package.json` itself, fnm uses sidecar version files); [`pixi`](clis/pixi/) (v0.67.2, BSD-3-Clause) — prefix-dev/pixi's Rust package manager that reuses the **conda-forge** binary ecosystem (CUDA, BLAS, ffmpeg, GDAL/PROJ, R, OpenJDK, Postgres clients) plus PyPI in one `pixi.lock` cross-platform lockfile (`linux-64` + `osx-arm64` + `osx-64` + `win-64` resolved together, no per-OS lockfile drift), Cargo-shaped UX (`pixi.toml` declares deps + tasks + features, `pixi run <task>` activates and runs), multi-environment composition via `[feature.dev]` / `[feature.cuda]` flags, file-fingerprint task `inputs:` / `outputs:` for skip-if-up-to-date — the right answer for ML / scientific / geospatial Python where pure-pip workflows ([`uv`](clis/uv/), `poetry`) hit "pip can't satisfy this OS dep" walls, replaces `conda` / `mamba` with a single Rust binary and lockfile-backed solver; [`kustomize`](clis/kustomize/) (v5.8.1, Apache-2.0) — kubernetes-sigs/kustomize's template-free Kubernetes manifest customizer where every YAML in the tree stays a valid `kubectl apply`-able object (no Go-template DSL, no `helm template` render step) and per-environment variation is layered as `overlays/staging/` + `overlays/prod/` `kustomization.yaml` files patching a shared `base/` via strategic-merge / JSON-6902 patches, name prefixes, namespace overrides, image-tag swaps, label injection, and content-hashed `configMapGenerator` / `secretGenerator` that auto-rolls consuming Deployments when a value changes — `kubectl apply -k overlays/prod` ships in every kubectl 1.14+, Argo CD and Flux speak it natively, and the editor's YAML LSP works on the inputs because they are still YAML.

Latest additions: [`vegeta`](clis/vegeta/) (v12.13.0, MIT) — tsenart/vegeta's HTTP load-testing tool that fixes **request rate** instead of concurrency (`-rate=200` schedules 200 req/s arrive at the target whether the server is healthy or melting — the only loading model that does not suffer from coordinated omission and the only one that produces apples-to-apples latency curves across runs), with a binary results stream that flows from `attack` into `report` / `plot` / `dump` / `encode` so one load run can be reported as text + JSON + interactive HTML latency plot + CSV without re-loading the target, plain-text targets file (`POST https://api/v1/foo\n@body.json`) so curl-shaped requests translate one-to-one, library-and-CLI parity (the same Go package `github.com/tsenart/vegeta/v12/lib` powers both), and a CI gate one-liner `vegeta attack ... | vegeta report -type=json | jq -e '.latencies."99th" < 250000000 and .success > 0.995'` — pairs with [`oha`](clis/oha/) (closed-model concurrency + real-time TUI for interactive exploration; vegeta for reproducible perf gates) and [`k6`](clis/k6/) (k6 when "scenario" is the unit of work, vegeta when "fire request X at rate Y" is) and orthogonal to [`grpcurl`](clis/grpcurl/) which exercises gRPC where vegeta loads HTTP/1.1 + HTTP/2; [`lefthook`](clis/lefthook/) (v1.13.6, MIT) — evilmartians/lefthook's polyglot Go-binary Git hooks manager that collapses the typical `husky` + `lint-staged` (Node) / `pre-commit` (Python) / `overcommit` (Ruby) split a polyglot monorepo accretes into one binary + one `lefthook.yml` with **parallel-by-default** hook execution (a 5-command pre-commit cuts from ~12 s serial to ~3 s parallel on a typical TS monorepo), file-glob filtering (`glob: "*.{ts,tsx}"`), staged-file injection (`{staged_files}`), `stage_fixed: true` re-staging (the `lint-staged` killer feature, but native), tags + skip rules (`tags: [backend]` plus `lefthook run pre-push --tags backend`), zero runtime dependency at hook execution (the npm / gem / pip packages just ship the platform binary, so CI images stay small and contributors skip the "install Node + Python + Ruby" step), and `LEFTHOOK=0 git commit ...` as the documented bypass that does *not* make `--no-verify` muscle memory — the right git-hook runner for repos that span JS + TS + Python + Ruby + Go + shell with the same idioms; [`trufflehog`](clis/trufflehog/) (v3.95.2, AGPL-3.0) — trufflesecurity/trufflehog's verified-secret scanner that runs each candidate string against the corresponding live API to confirm it is currently valid before flagging (~800 detectors across AWS / GCP / GitHub / Slack / Stripe / Twilio / Datadog / OpenAI / Anthropic / Postman / Notion / etc.; `aws sts get-caller-identity` for AWS, `/user` for GitHub, `auth.test` for Slack, `/v1/charges?limit=1` for Stripe), so `--only-verified` turns "800 regex hits to triage" into "8 live secrets to rotate now" — dropping ~90–99 % of regex matches on a typical legacy repo and leaving an actionable list instead of a multi-week audit; same Go binary scans local filesystem, git (with full history walk), GitHub repo + org + issues + PRs + gists, GitLab, Bitbucket, S3, GCS, Azure Blob, Docker images, container registries, Postman workspaces, Jira, Confluence, Slack workspaces, Elasticsearch indices, Jenkins / Travis / CircleCI logs, SQL dumps — one source-agnostic engine, one JSON output schema for SIEM ingest, one `--fail` exit code for the CI gate; pairs with regex-only scanners like `gitleaks` on every commit (cheap + fast) plus `trufflehog --only-verified` on a nightly schedule (broader surface, more accurate signal), and complements [`age`](clis/age/) / [`sops`](clis/sops/) (those manage secrets you keep on purpose; trufflehog catches the ones that slipped past); the AGPL-3.0 licence is unrestricted for using the binary against your own repos / cloud accounts from CI but has obligations if you embed the source into a hosted scanner you offer to third parties — and verification means the binary *will* call out to AWS / GitHub / Slack / Stripe with each candidate credential, so air-gapped scans need `--no-verification` and a higher false-positive tolerance.

Latest additions: [`mdbook`](clis/mdbook/) (v0.5.2, MPL-2.0) — rust-lang/mdBook's static-site generator for book-shaped technical docs: the existence proof is the entire Rust documentation library (TRPL, Reference, Cargo Book, Rustonomicon, Embedded Book) and the win is that `SUMMARY.md`, a single nested-bullet Markdown file, is the source of truth for chapter ordering / sidebar / prev-next / breadcrumb (reorganising the book is editing one file, no front-matter `weight:` fields scattered across 80 chapters), `{{#include ../src/lib.rs:42:60}}` directives pull code samples from real source files so docs cannot drift past a line range without a build error, `mdbook test` actually compiles + runs every Rust code block in the book against your project, and the output is a static-by-construction tarball (HTML + CSS + small JS bundle for search and theme, no Node runtime, no PHP, no server, deployable with `aws s3 sync` / GitHub Pages / `caddy file-server` / `python -m http.server`) — the right "publish a multi-chapter handbook" tool when MkDocs's Material theme ecosystem and Sphinx's autodoc are both more than you need; pairs with [`marker`](clis/marker/) (use `marker` to ingest a legacy PDF spec into Markdown, edit it, then `mdbook build` to publish the modernised version) and replaces ad-hoc concatenated-README docs sites; [`stylua`](clis/stylua/) (v2.4.1, MPL-2.0) — JohnnyMorganz/StyLua's Rust formatter for the entire Lua family (5.1 / 5.2 / 5.3 / 5.4 / Luau / Roblox-Luau, selected via `--syntax` flag or `stylua.toml`) that fixes the historical fragmentation across game-engine forks (Roblox/Luau, LuaJIT/OpenResty, vanilla/Neovim plugins, Solar2D/mobile games) by being the one binary every community converged on: AST round-trip via the hand-rolled `full_moon` parser (no regex munging, no breakage on multiline strings or comment-laden tables, `stylua | stylua` is a fixed point), `--check` mode for CI, stdin → stdout for editor-on-save, ~6 MB static binary, formats a 50 KLOC repo in well under a second, default formatter recommended by Roblox developer docs / Neovim plugin community / Lune runtime — the `gofmt` / `rustfmt` / `prettier` of Lua, with a small knob set (column width, indent kind, quote style, call-parens policy) and the same "no, that is the canonical shape" posture the maintainer takes against most "let me configure X" requests; [`biome`](clis/biome/) (v2.4.13, MIT/Apache-2.0) — biomejs/biome's unified Rust formatter + linter for JS / TS / JSX / TSX / JSON / CSS / GraphQL that collapses the typical Prettier + ESLint + `eslint-config-airbnb` + half-a-dozen `eslint-plugin-*` + `@typescript-eslint/parser` + `lint-staged` + `husky` sprawl (~30 dev-deps, 4 config files, 3 caches) into one binary, one `biome.json`, one CST-preserving parser pass that the formatter and ~280 lint rules share: 10–30× faster than the ESLint+Prettier combo it replaces (50 KLOC TS monorepo: ~25 s → ~1 s), >97 % Prettier-output-identical so switching does not produce a "reformatted everything" megacommit, sub-10 ms format-on-save, `biome lsp-proxy` is the LSP server (no Node packages or plugin chain to install in the editor), `biome ci` for CI, `biome check --staged --write` for pre-commit — the JS/TS-side analogue of [`ruff`](clis/ruff/) for Python (same Rust-binary + formatter+linter + ~30× speedup + single-config shape), distinct from [`dprint`](clis/dprint/) (formatter-only, multi-language plugin model) and [`oxc`](clis/oxc/) (lower-level toolkit; `oxlint` is the linter alone).

Earlier additions: [`hyperfine`](clis/hyperfine/) (v1.20.0, MIT/Apache-2.0) — sharkdp's statistically rigorous CLI benchmarking harness that turns "is change A actually faster than change B" from `time foo` eyeballed three times into `hyperfine foo bar` printing `bar ran 1.43 ± 0.04 times faster than foo` with warmup, outlier detection, parameter scans (`--parameter-scan threads 1 16`), and Markdown / JSON / CSV / asciidoc export for CI gating; [`starship`](clis/starship/) (v1.25.0, ISC) — starship/starship's cross-shell prompt: one Rust binary for ten shells, ~70 modules detecting git / language version / Kubernetes / cloud profile / direnv / mise state, configured by one `~/.config/starship.toml` so the prompt definition lives in one place instead of forked-and-drifted bash / zsh / fish snippets, with `<10 ms` render budget held via async detection + per-render stat cache; [`htmlq`](clis/htmlq/) (v0.4.0, MIT) — mgdm/htmlq's `jq`-shaped Unix filter for HTML on the `html5ever` parser, full CSS3 selectors, `--text` / `--attribute href` / `--remove-nodes` / `--base URL` flags so `curl -s URL \| htmlq -a href 'a.story'` is a one-liner where the Python `requests + bs4` equivalent is a script.

> **Caveat.** Licenses, model lists, and feature flags drift. Each subdirectory
> README pins a "as of" date — treat it as a snapshot, not a contract.

## How to read a per-CLI README

Every `clis/<name>/README.md` answers the same nine questions in the same order:

1. Install footprint (binary size, deps, OS support)
2. License
3. Models supported
4. MCP support
5. Sub-agent model
6. Telemetry stance (on by default? opt-out? opt-in?)
7. Prompt-cache strategy
8. Hot keybinds (TUI / REPL)
9. Killer feature, weakness, when to choose

This makes side-by-side reading trivial — open two READMEs, scroll in lockstep.

## Contributing

Issues and PRs welcome. Two rules:
- **No marketing copy.** If you can't run the CLI yourself, don't write the entry.
- **Cite versions.** "As of v0.x.y" beats "as of today" every time.
